# How to split Ordinals / Runes / Alkanes / BTC / FB? | UniSat

UniSat UTXO Management Tool: [https://unisat.io/utxo](https://unisat.io/utxo)

Splitting UTXOs to different addresses with custom amounts, or breaking large UTXOs into smaller ones, can help improve asset flexibility, prevent asset mixing, and enable faster, smoother transactions.

UniSat UTXO Management Tool now supports easy UTXO splitting for:

*   Alkanes Assets
    
*   Ordinals
    
*   Runes
    
*   BTC (on Bitcoin Mainnet) / FB (on Fractal Mainnet)
    

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-split-ordinals-runes-alkanes-btc-fb#how-to-split-your-utxos)

How to Split Your UTXOs？

Let's take Split Alkanes as an example. Please note that the Split process for Ordinals, Runes, and BTC may vary slightly. You can check the specific details on each asset's Split page.

**⚠ Always double-check before pressing that confirm button!**

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FAzBE4c5S6Z0Cun6o2wtB%252Fsplit.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D386b9a7b-b44c-4164-b236-4e8fac3917c7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1b718454&sv=2)

**🔸 Alkanes:**

*   **Auto split:** Select and split Alkanes UTXOs to a designated receive address.
    
*   **Manual split:** Select and split Alkanes UTXOs to multiple receive addresses with custom amounts - total control.
    

_Note:_

*   _UTXOs containing mixed assets cannot be operated on._
    
*   _Only UTXOs of the same Alkanes tickers can be operated on._
    

**🔸 Ordinals:**

*   **Batch send** up to 500 inscriptions/collections/name/ brc-20 transfer UTXOs to a designated address to save time and fees.
    
*   **Efficiently split** a UTXO containing multiple inscriptions into separate ones.
    

_Note: UTXOs that contain mixed assets (e.g., both Ordinals and Runes) cannot be operated on._

**🔸 Runes:**

*   **Auto split:** Select and split Runes UTXOs to one designated receive address.
    
*   **Manual split:** Select and split Runes UTXOs to multiple receive addresses with custom amounts.
    

_Note:_

*   _UTXOs containing mixed assets cannot be operated on._
    
*   _Only UTXOs of the same Runes ticker can be operated on._
    

**🔸 BTC / FB:**

*   **Auto split:** Select and split large BTC/FB UTXOs into multiple smaller UTXOs of equal size to a designated receive address.
    
*   **Manual split:** Select & split one or more BTC/FB UTXOs and batch send them to multiple receive addresses with custom amounts.
    

_Note: BTC/FB UTXOs that are locked cannot be operated on in this tab. Once selected, all buttons will be disabled._

[PreviousHow to reclaim BTC/FB trapped in useless inscription UTXOs](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-reclaim-btc-fb-trapped-in-useless-inscription-utxos)
[NextHow to batch send Ordinals / Runes / Alkanes / BTC / FB?](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-batch-send-ordinals-runes-alkanes-btc-fb)

Last updated 18 days ago

# .unisat Names | UniSat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals/.unisat-names#so-what-is-.unisat)

So what is .unisat?

It's easy to explain what .unisat is - **.unisat follows exactly the same protocol as .sats** ([the documentation](https://docs.sats.id/)
), except it produces accumulative benefits to your account in UniSat Products.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FQTJTX6kQTf5ZFGWioscB%252F1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7325e080-1560-4a9b-be41-89ffa88091c4&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=68e63d3c&sv=2)

Just like what happens to .sats

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals/.unisat-names#inscribe-.unisat-directly)

Inscribe .unisat directly

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FVXIkRJ3SD5RNWYwEjUj7%252F3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D05e4fb41-06a1-43b2-8de0-1c0861eb8508&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8f5745b8&sv=2)

the first class tab of UniSat Inscribe for .unisat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals/.unisat-names#search-for-.unisat-directly)

Search for .unisat directly

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FpzInog7qAKLinNtdIfEI%252F4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da75874e1-8092-46d3-b829-2cfcc8c50de8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=860410d0&sv=2)

the first class tab of UniSat Search for .unisat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals/.unisat-names#accumulative-benefits)

Accumulative benefits

Specifically for UniSat Inscribe, one .unisat in your address produces a 1% discount. There are five .unisat names at most that take effect in one payment.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FLIT1wrmUd9Je2gZLTpj8%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd4432a79-038b-47e7-8a45-97145f8066d5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1ff36780&sv=2)

Two .unisat names produce 2% discounts.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals/.unisat-names#extra-resources)

Extra resources

*   For a complete reference, please check out [the documentation of .sats here](https://docs.sats.id/)
    .
    
*   For a video tutorial, please check out the tutorial about inscribing multiple .unisat here.
    

Yes, it's that easy.

# Green Channel User Guide | UniSat

Earlier, we launched brc20-Swap testing on the Bitcoin mainnet, where some users deposited assets. Now, these users can transfer their assets to PizzaSwap through the Green Channel, as shown below.

PizzaSwap: [https://fractal.unisat.io/swap](https://fractal.unisat.io/swap)

brc20-Swap on Bitcoin mainnet: [https://unisat.io/swap](https://unisat.io/swap)

**Step-by-Step Instructions:**

1.  **Connect Wallet & Access brc-20 Swap:**
    
    *   Open your wallet and navigate to the brc-20 swap page.
        
    *   Click on "My Module Assets."
        
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F3fnrsNNhIlTLjWfOYiQ3%252F11.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd93e71ea-67d5-4c6c-9083-19aace4722e0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9365d0e0&sv=2)

1.  **Select Assets to Bridge:**
    

*   Choose the asset you want to bridge.
    
*   Click "Bridge" to initiate the transfer. Since you need SATS as the gas fee, make sure to bridge your SATS last.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FjjuQB18QVyi4JbJ3Yk3N%252F22.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dea65a53f-1a2d-402a-818a-e8fc3de92dd7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8f05417&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FMFlaoTAQBFQLyxJUp9GY%252F33.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8451c0da-8322-4499-afab-94de3da9e942&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8c749029&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F8aGKO6QeSkKl6PWaOva0%252F44.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De7bef2e1-f8a8-45dc-9e3f-cef4a436aaf6&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=77ab6164&sv=2)

1.  **Monitor Processing Status:**
    

*   Keep an eye on the transaction status. Once marked as "completed," you can check PizzaSwap for your transferred assets.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FddVQ9jd0125vGVeNWaG6%252F55.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5a49c4fb-9be5-40b2-a347-cb116a0a3a71&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4ba9d788&sv=2)

1.  **Check Assets in PizzaSwap:**
    

*   Go to PizzaSwap: [https://fractal.unisat.io/swap](https://fractal.unisat.io/swap)
     and access "My Assets on PizzaSwap" to verify the arrival of your assets.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FXPaOGzHzvP9QCGnBwrZ6%252F66.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1c4a6871-bd7a-4a5a-9e92-72d395f4701a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6cdbe7c4&sv=2)

This guide helps you navigate the Green Channel process smoothly, ensuring a quick and efficient asset transfer.

[PreviousHow to interact with PizzaSwap？](https://docs.unisat.io/pizzaswap/how-to-interact-with-pizzaswap)
[NextGuides for withdrawing your assets from PizzaSwap or brc20-swap](https://docs.unisat.io/pizzaswap/guides-for-withdrawing-your-assets-from-pizzaswap-or-brc20-swap)

# UniSat Titles | UniSat

UniSat Titles are your personal collection of digital medals that celebrate your journey in the UniSat community!

Each Title marks a moment when you helped Bitcoin grow and thrive. As you collect more, you'll unlock exciting new ways to earn benefits from UniSat and our partners, starting with exclusive allocations in UniSat Drops.

Claim your titles here by connecting your wallet to verify eligibility: [https://unisat.io/address/my\_title](https://unisat.io/address/my_title)

There is no fee involved in claiming Titles. Titles are awarded for free and exist off-chain, making them non-transferable and non-tradable digital achievements.

💡This list keeps track of all available Titles, and will continue to be updated as more Titles are released.

*   **Diamond Hand**
    
    *   WZRD (brc-20) Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired/minted and held of any amount of $wzrd for more than 90 days consecutive
            
        
    *   Bitcoin Wizard (NFT) Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired/minted and held a Bitcoin Wizard for more than 90 days consecutive
            
        
    *   PIZZA (brc-20) Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired/minted and held of any amount of $pizza for more than 90 days consecutive
            
        
    *   UniSat OG Pass Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired/minted and held a UniSat OG Pass for more than 90 days consecutive
            
        
    *   Prime Access Pass Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired and held a UniSat Prime Access Pass for more than 90 consecutive days.
            
        
    *   Early Access Pass Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired and held a UniSat Early Access Pass for more than 90 consecutive days.
            
        
    *   UniSat Emblem Diamond Hand
        
        *   Acquired and held a UniSat Emblem for more than 90 consecutive days.
            
        
    
*   **Product Pioneer**
    
    *   UniSat Points Hodler (>500)
        
        *   Collected more than 500 UniSat points, on Fractal and Bitcoin network combined.
            
        
    *   Early Contributor to brc-20 Swap
        
        *   Addresses eligible for early access to brc-20 swap module on Bitcoin during testing and Alpha Launch
            
        
    *   Fractal Inaugural Voters
        
        *   Voted in the first Fractal Vote and first Fractal Eco vote(include all 7 eco projects vote)
            
        
    

*   **Community Builder**
    
    *   UniSat Community Champion
        
        *   Received any UniSat emblem for participating in community events and still hold the emblem in the wallet
            
        
    *   Bitcoin Tech Carnival 2025
        
        *   Physical attendees of the Bitcoin Tech Carnival event during Consensus 2025 who has submitted their address during registration.
            
        
    *   Fractal Christmas Carnival 2024 Stamp Collector's Club
        
        *   Collected all 12 stamps in Fractal Christmas Carnival 2024
            
        
    *   Fractal Community Champion
        
        *   Winners in Fractal Bitcoin Community Events
            
        
    *   UniSat Discord Contributor
        
        *   Community members who earned the Community Supporter role in UniSat’s official Discord.
            
        
    

📍 Titles will be continuously added and adjusted based on our ongoing plans and arrangements.

You can view the details of different titles at: [https://unisat.io/address/my\_title](https://unisat.io/address/my_title)

# UniSat Points | UniSat

**What are UniSat Points?**

UniSat Points is a tool designed by UniSat to count the number of user inscriptions and calculate how many users participate in UniSat interactions.

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-points#points-can-be-earned-through-inscribing)

**Points can be earned through i**nscribing


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**How to Earn UniSat Points on Bitcoin mainnet？**

Points can be earned when using the inscribe service **and a service fee is charged**. The specific rules for earning points are as follows:

> _No points will be awarded for fee-free inscriptions._

*   1 ≤ Inscribing quantity in a batch ≤ 4 👉 Earn **1 Point**
    
*   5 ≤ Inscribing quantity in a batch ≤ 20 👉 Earn **2 Points**
    
*   21 ≤ Inscribing quantity in a batch ≤ 32 👉 Earn **3 Points**
    
*   33 ≤ Inscribing quantity in a batch ≤ 1000 👉 Earn **4 Points**
    

_The points are accumulated on the receiving address of the inscription, not the payment address._

**How to Earn UniSat Points on Fractal Bitcoin Mainnet?**

*   During Fractal InscribeFest 22 July -30 September, every 2500 inscribing quantity = **1 Point**
    

_(Batch Minting: Up to 1000 inscriptions per batch ) The points are accumulated on the receiving address of the inscription, not the payment address._

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-points#points-can-be-earned-through-consolidating-useless-inscriptions-utxos)

**Points can be earned through c**onsolidating **u**seless inscriptions UTXOs


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FiqiAS3uDqSOhFRRK3JGY%252F22.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D433ebb50-9093-4455-b771-5106d059d1ac&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5b25c6b7&sv=2)

**How to Earn UniSat Points by Consolidating Useless Inscriptions UTXOs:**

*   **On Bitcoin Mainnet** (via [UTXO Management Tool](https://unisat.io/utxo)
    ) - _Points are awarded only when a service fee is incurred._
    
    *   50 ≤ X < 300 👉 Earn **1 Point**
        
    *   300 ≤ X < 500 👉 Earn **2 Points**
        
    *   X = 500 👉 Earn **3 Points**
        
    

👉 Points are awarded based on the number of UTXOs you consolidate(**X**):

**How to Earn UniSat Points by Consolidating Useless Inscriptions UTXOs:**

*   **On Fractal Mainnet** (via [UTXO Management Tool](https://fractal.unisat.io/utxo)
    )
    
    *   X = 500 👉 Earn **1 Point**
        
    

Points are awarded based on the number of UTXOs you consolidate (**X**):

# UniSat Credits | UniSat

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-credits#id-5b65)

What is Credits?


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Credit is a ‘virtual’ FB that can be used towards service fee offset and other benefits across our products. It is designed to reward users who have been long-term supporters and have made significant contributions to our network.

Please note that **Credit is not an on-chain asset. It is non-transferable, non-tradable, and can only be used within the UniSat ecosystem.**

The first batch of eligible addresses that will receive the Credits includes miners that have successfully mined blocks during Fractal Testnet, early testers of brc20 swap on Bitcoin mainnet, and users who had difficulties with claim during the Fractal Bitcoin Mainnet Bootstrap Program.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FKE1lGQFz3B5P5mDHR1qc%252F1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbb45f5df-97aa-4782-b952-a3f3af944f04&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=db1d26fd&sv=2)

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-credits#id-6221)

How Does Credits Work?


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Credits can be used to offset Rollup Fee on PizzaSwap and to offset service fees in UniSat Inscribe, replacing the FB or BTC you would typically use. When trading on PizzaSwap or inscribing, simply select “Credits” for rollup fee deductions.

Over time, we plan to expand the use of these Credits to other UniSat services, such as UniSat Inscribe, UniSat Marketplace, and other features in the future.

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-credits#id-6dfb)

Eligibility for Credits


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users eligible to receive **Goodwill Credit** include:

1.  **Initially eligible users who were later unable to claim during the Fractal Bitcoin Mainnet Bootstrap Program**
    

*   90FB worth of credit in total for each address, with 15FB credits distributed monthly over six consecutive months.
    

**2\. Miner addresses that participated in Fractal Testnet mining and successfully mined blocks:**

*   Credit will be distributed based on the total number of successful blocks mined. Each block is worth 0.5 FB. For addresses that mined fewer than 40 blocks (inclusive), a minimum threshold of 20 FB worth of credit will be granted. The maximum cap is 1500 FB per address. Addresses with 0 blocks mined will not be eligible for this benefit.
    
*   For addresses eligible to receive more than 20 FB worth of Credits, the Credits will be distributed monthly with a cap of 20 FB worth of Credits each month until the full amount is dispersed.
    
*   If you are a Fractal testnet miner who has mined blocks but has not received any credits, please contact us and create a ticket on Discord [http://discord.gg/unisat](http://discord.gg/unisat)
    

**3\. Addresses that participated in early testing of the brc20-swap on the Bitcoin Mainnet:**

*   20 FB worth of credit for each address, distributed monthly over six consecutive months.
    

**4\. Addresses with 1,000 or more UniSat Points:**

*   If you have 1000 or more UniSat Points, you’re eligible to receive a total of 60FB worth of credit, with 10 FB Credits distributed monthly over six consecutive months.
    

**Note:** Monthly Credits not claimed in the current month will expire when next month’s Credits become available.

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/unisat-credits#d3ea)

How to Get Started with the Credit?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  If you qualify, please visit [https://unisat.io/address/credit](https://unisat.io/address/credit)
     or connect your wallet and click on “Credits” to claim it.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FdLztanjPZHTuoUXgCAAj%252F33.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D06b8c896-4bcd-4c76-a8e0-4e510d1fb2ce&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e442e6a3&sv=2)

2\. When trading on PizzaSwap or inscribing, select “Credits” for rollup fee deductions.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FS8P8XI3PbUSjgjLEM8wk%252F44.avif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df02a8820-48af-4d2e-8fa5-d9a701bd967b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=59b5ef78&sv=2)

# What is Signet? | UniSat

Signet is a Bitcoin test network designed for developers to test their applications in a controlled environment. Unlike the traditional testnet, Signet doesn't rely on miners. Instead, blocks are created by a trusted party, providing predictable and consistent block times.

**What are the Key Features?**

*   Blocks are created every 10 minutes by a trusted party, ensuring consistency.
    
*   Mimics the mainnet environment closely, making it ideal for development and testing.
    
*   Endorsed and supported by Bitcoin Core, widely adopted by the developer community.
    

**How is Signet Different from Testnet?**

*   Testnet relies on miners, leading to unpredictable block times, while Signet uses a trusted party, ensuring consistent block production.
    
*   Signet offers a more stable environment for testing compared to the often erratic testnet.
    
*   Signet is preferred by developers for its reliability and consistency, whereas testnet is used for broader testing purposes.
    

More information:

https://bitcoinops.org/en/topics/signet/

# Understanding Bitcoin Address Types | UniSat

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-1.-legacy)

1\. **Legacy**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Legacy transactions, also known as Pay-to-Public-Key-Hash (P2PKH), represent the original and most common address format.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with the number "1."
    
*   Legacy transactions are less space-efficient and can lead to higher transaction fees due to their larger size.
    

Example Legacy Address: `1A1zP1eP5QGefi2DMPTfTL5SLmv7DivfNa`

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-2.-nested-segwit-p2sh-p2wpkh)

**2\. Nested SegWit (P2SH-P2WPKH)**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Nested SegWit, or Pay-to-Witness-Public-Key-Hash (P2SH-P2WPKH), is an interim solution that combines features of both Legacy and Native SegWit.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with the number "3."
    
*   It allows Legacy wallets to send funds to SegWit addresses while still benefiting from lower fees.
    

Example Nested SegWit Address: `3J98t1WpEZ73CNmQviecrnyiWrnqRhWNLy`

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-3.-native-segwit-bech32)

**3\. Native SegWit (bech32)**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Native SegWit, or bech32, represents an improvement over Legacy transactions in terms of scalability and reduced transaction fees.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with "bc1."
    
*   Native SegWit uses a more efficient scripting language (Segregated Witness) to reduce transaction size.
    

Example Native SegWit Address: `bc1qar0srrr7xfkvy5l643lydnw9re59gtzzwf5mdq`

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-4.-taproot)

**4\. Taproot**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Taproot is the latest Bitcoin address format designed to enhance privacy, scalability, and scripting capabilities. Addresses in this format start with "bc1p."
    
*   Taproot allows the aggregation of multiple signatures, making complex transactions more efficient and cost-effective.
    

Example Taproot Address: `bc1puaz84y65g0jh7zlhwv9vwhuu3se8ldf82lk5ca6zru6kdny2zvws69x6jd`

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#our-recommendation)

Our recommendation


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For UniSat Wallet users, we suggest choosing Taproot or Native Segwit. Taproot offers substantial cost savings on transaction fees, but not all CEX platforms support it. Native SegWit has better compatibility with CEX platforms.

[PreviousHow does Bitcoin work?](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/how-does-bitcoin-work)
[NextWhat is Signet?](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/what-is-signet)

# Glossary | UniSat

**Blockchain**

A decentralized and distributed ledger that records all transactions across a network of computers. The Bitcoin blockchain is the founding technology that enables the existence of cryptocurrency.

**Cryptocurrency**

Digital or virtual currency that uses cryptography for security. Bitcoin is a prime example of a cryptocurrency.

**Private Key**

A secret cryptographic key that allows the owner to access and control their cryptocurrency holdings. It must be kept confidential to maintain the security of the wallet.

**Public Key**

A cryptographic key derived from the private key and used to generate the wallet address. It is shared publicly and is used for receiving cryptocurrency.

**Wallet Address**

A unique identifier associated with a cryptocurrency wallet, used to receive funds. It is derived from the public key.

**Seed Phrase (or Secret Recovery Phrase)**

A series of words that serve as a backup for the private key. It is essential for wallet recovery in case of loss or device failure.

**Multi-Signature (Multisig)**

A security feature requiring multiple private keys to authorize a Bitcoin transaction. It adds an extra layer of protection against unauthorized access.

**Hardware Wallet**

A physical device designed to securely store private keys offline, reducing the risk of online hacking.

**Software Wallet**

A digital application or program that allows users to store and manage their cryptocurrency. UniSat Wallet is an example of a software wallet.

**Decentralized Finance (DeFi)**

A financial ecosystem built on blockchain technology, aiming to recreate traditional financial systems with decentralized, open-source alternatives.

**Smart Contracts**

Self-executing contracts with the terms of the agreement directly written into code. They run on blockchain networks like Ethereum, facilitating trustless and automated transactions.

**Transaction Fee**

The fee paid to miners to process and verify transactions on the blockchain. It varies based on network congestion and transaction complexity.

**Non-Fungible Token (NFT)**

Unique digital assets representing ownership or proof of authenticity for items like art, collectibles, or virtual real estate.

**Cold Storage**

Keeping private keys or seed phrases in an offline, secure environment to protect against online hacking attempts.

**Peer-to-Peer (P2P)**

Transactions that occur directly between two parties without the need for intermediaries.

**Confirmation**

The process of validating a transaction on the blockchain by multiple nodes, ensuring its accuracy and security.

**KYC (Know Your Customer)**

Verification processes to confirm the identity of wallet owners, complying with regulatory requirements.

**HD Wallet (Hierarchical Deterministic Wallet)**

A wallet that generates a hierarchical tree of keys from a single seed, making it easier to manage multiple addresses.

**Web3**

The next generation of the internet, focused on decentralized protocols and applications, including blockchain-based technologies.

[PreviousWhat is Signet?](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/what-is-signet)
[NextOrdinals](https://docs.unisat.io/ordinals)

# How does Bitcoin work? | UniSat

At the heart of Bitcoin lies the blockchain, a distributed ledger system that records every transaction ever made. This public ledger ensures transparency and immutability, preventing fraudulent activity. Transactions are initiated by users with digital signatures, verified by miners, and then added to the blockchain in blocks.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/how-does-bitcoin-work#securing-and-validating-the-network)

Securing and Validating the Network

Mining is the process of verifying and adding new transactions to the blockchain. It also serves the essential role of securing the network through a computational puzzle called proof-of-work (PoW).

**Mempool**

New transactions are broadcast to the network by users. These transactions can involve sending Bitcoin, creating new contracts, or changing existing ones. The transactions are temporarily stored in a distributed memory pool, accessible by all nodes on the network. Fees act as a digital tipping system, guiding miners towards transactions that promise greater rewards.

**Block Creation**

Miners compete to collect and group unconfirmed transactions into blocks. Each block has a limited capacity, so miners choose transactions that maximize their potential reward. Miners add a "coinbase" transaction to each block, which is essentially a reward for themselves for successfully creating the block.

**Hashing**

Hashing is a cryptographic function that takes any data as input and generates a unique, fixed-length output. In the context of Bitcoin mining, the input consists of the block header, including the previous block's hash, timestamp, and Merkle root. Miners use specialized hardware called ASICs to perform billions of calculations per second, attempting to find a hash that starts with a certain number of zeros. It is often described as "solving a complex mathematical puzzle". This difficulty is adjusted automatically to maintain the average block creation time at approximately 10 minutes.

**Block Validation**

Once a miner finds a valid hash, they broadcast the new block to the network. Other nodes on the network verify the block by:

*   Recalculating the hash and ensuring it meets the difficulty requirements.
    
*   Validating all transactions within the block.
    
*   Checking the block header information for accuracy and consistency.
    

If the block is valid, it is added to the blockchain, and the successful miner receives their reward in Bitcoin. Blocks are considered confirmed after a certain number of subsequent blocks have been added to the chain. This typically requires six confirmations, making it very difficult to alter or tamper with previously confirmed blocks.

[PreviousWhat is Bitcoin?](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/what-is-bitcoin)
[NextUnderstanding Bitcoin Address Types](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types)

Last updated 1 month ago

# Fractal Bitcoin | UniSat

Fractal Bitcoin is the only Bitcoin scaling solution that uses the Bitcoin Core code itself to recursively scale unlimited layers on top of the world’s most-secure and-held blockchain. UniSat, as one of the core contributors to Fractal Bitcoin, participates in the development and maintenance of its core infrastructure — supporting Fractal’s sustainable growth and long-term stability.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin#fractal-bitcoin-a-truly-native-scaling-solution)

Fractal Bitcoin - A truly native scaling solution

Fractal is the first instance of a virtualization methodology applied to Bitcoin in the world. Fractal gradually extends the Bitcoin blockchain into a scalable computing system without breaking consistency with the Bitcoin main chain.

*   **Native**
    
    Recursive scaling of Bitcoin Core code itself — without any foreign constructs — ensures consistent and unlimited scaling, and native support of current infrastructure (e.g. wallets).
    
*   **Fast**
    
    Block confirmation times are 30 seconds or less, with 20x increase in capacity per layer.
    
*   **Dynamic Scaling**
    
    On-chain interactions can scale up and down as demand changes; it acts as a dynamic “blockspace load balancer” and reduces congestion on any specific layer. This enables internet-scale applications on the Bitcoin blockchain, as has never been done before.
    
*   **Consistent**
    
    Due to each layer’s self-replicating consistency with the main chain, on-chain consensus is preserved. Any layer’s transactions/hashes can be traced back to the source on the Bitcoin chain, without the risks of forks or shards involved.
    
*   **Easy**
    
    Additionally, due to this consistency across layers, assets can be directly transferred from layer to another without the need for additional relays.
    

Learn more: [https://fractalbitcoin.io/fractal-primer](https://fractalbitcoin.io/fractal-primer)

[PreviousFAQ](https://docs.unisat.io/alkanes/faq)
[NextRunes on Fractal](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/runes-on-fractal)

# Name recognized and resolved | UniSat

A name can be recognized and resolved to an address by an inscription. Each name have a unique inscription associated with it.

Once a name inscription is inscribed or transferred, it is only resolved to an address after achieving 3 confirmations. At present, we support the following name inscription protocols, with more domains being gradually made available based on user demand.

# How to Transfer $BABY to a Cosmos Wallet | UniSat

If you previously used UniSat Wallet to participate in Babylon’s staking, you can transfer your $BABY airdrop to a Cosmos wallet for easier management and further operations.

This guide is for reference only. For more details about $BABY, please refer to the official Babylon website: [https://babylonlabs.io/](https://babylonlabs.io/)

**Step 1: Prepare a Cosmos Wallet**

*   Choose a Cosmos-compatible wallet that supports $BABY, such as Leap or Keplr.
    
*   After creating your wallet account, switch the network to Babylon Network.
    
*   Click on Receive, and copy your BBN address.
    

(This example uses Leap wallet.)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FHx0gxIc2otI8GCNQjlBe%252Fleap.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D78a65b0d-96d0-4332-a36d-3adf73f0e00b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d3ec1fed&sv=2)

**Step 2: Open Your UniSat Wallet**

*   Open your UniSat Wallet, and switch to the **BTC Mainnet network**.
    
*   Go to the Discover page, and find the **Babylon** entry.
    

Ensure that your UniSat Extension Wallet is updated to the latest version v1.6.1. Click the link to download or update: [https://unisat.io/download](https://unisat.io/download)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FD8PQsKARKUmx9Oo7nlnm%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dcb5b0457-0e0c-4489-bf98-99e6f618e81b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d1b4500b&sv=2)

**Step 3: Go to the Babylon Page**

*   On the Babylon page, you will see the Claimed BABY section. Click the **Transfer** button in the Claimed BABY section.
    
*   Follow the on-screen prompts to click **Transfer $BABY to Cosmos Wallet**, then click **Confirm** to confirm your action.
    
*   In the transfer interface, input the BBN wallet address you created in Step 1 as the receiving address for your $BABY, and enter the transfer amount.
    
*   Once you confirm the information is correct, click Next, then sign the transaction to complete the transfer of your $BABY to your Cosmos wallet address.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FcltHR24FOAXOJew3VMbG%252Fcosmos.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd7a258e4-160b-493a-91b9-7fa7860238e0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b63fbcea&sv=2)

**Additional Notes:**

*   Ensure that your Cosmos wallet is set up to support $BABY transfers and is connected to the Babylon Network.
    
*   If the Babylon DApp entry is not showing in your UniSat wallet, please ensure your wallet is updated to the latest version.
    
*   Babylon is a third-party project. Please make sure you fully understand the associated risks and terms before processing.
    
*   If you encounter any issues, please reach out to us via our Discord: [http://discord.gg/unisat](http://discord.gg/unisat)
    

* * *

If you participated in Babylon BTC staking Cap 2 or Cap 3, please stay tuned for future updates from the Babylon team.

* * *

Download the latest UniSat Extension or update: [https://unisat.io/download](https://unisat.io/download)

* * *

* * *

 to view the correct staked amount. This display issue will be fixed in the next version — thank you for your patience!

# Runes on Fractal | UniSat

Runes on Fractal follows the same set of rules as the Bitcoin mainnet. If you're familiar with the runes protocol on Bitcoin, you'll find that the structure and functionalities on Fractal are fully aligned with it. Here's what you need to know:

**1\. Same Rules as Bitcoin Mainnet**

The Runes protocol on Fractal follows the same fundamental rules as on Bitcoin, with all phases completed within one halving cycle (it takes 4 years on Bitcoin, and takes 2 years on Fractal)

There are 12 phases on both networks. Therefore, any single phase takes 120 days on Bitcoin, and 60 days on Fractal.

**2\. Ticker Names on Fractal**

On the Fractal mainnet, all Runes tickers are displayed in **lowercase** letters.

For more detailed information on the Runes protocol, you can refer to the official documentation here: [Runes Protocol Documentation](https://docs.ordinals.com/runes.html)
.

[PreviousFractal Bitcoin](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin)
[NextHow to Etch Runes?](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/runes-on-fractal/how-to-etch-runes)

# What is Bitcoin? | UniSat

Instead of relying on a central bank to issue and manage the currency, Bitcoin utilizes a distributed ledger, the blockchain, to record all transactions in a transparent and immutable manner. This ledger is maintained by a network of computers, known as miners, who compete to solve complex cryptographic puzzles. By solving these puzzles, miners not only verify transactions but also earn Bitcoin rewards, ensuring the network's security and incentivizing further participation.

Beyond its unique infrastructure, Bitcoin offers individuals a new form of digital currency. Transactions are conducted quickly and securely, without the need for intermediaries or cross-border restrictions. This opens up a world of possibilities, from sending money across the globe to making online purchases with newfound ease.

However, Bitcoin's decentralized nature also presents its own set of challenges. Scalability remains a hurdle, as the current network struggles to handle large volumes of transactions. Additionally, the absence of central oversight raises concerns about regulatory uncertainty.

Despite these challenges, Bitcoin's impact on the financial world is undeniable. It has paved the way for a new era of digital currencies and decentralized finance, sparking innovation and challenging traditional financial systems. With its limited supply of 21 million coins, Bitcoin's value is primarily driven by market demand, leading to significant price fluctuations. This volatility, coupled with its revolutionary technology and potential for future growth, continues to attract investors and enthusiasts alike.

[PreviousBitcoin](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin)
[NextHow does Bitcoin work?](https://docs.unisat.io/academy/bitcoin/how-does-bitcoin-work)

# How to Etch Runes? | UniSat

You may visit [https://unisat.io/runes/inscribe](https://unisat.io/runes/inscribe)
 to get the page.

Input the parameters as needed.

_**For example**_：

The _**Rune**_ Name is EVERYONE.LOVES.NATURE.FOREVER,

_**Symbol**_ is E,

It is _**Mintable**_, and _**Amount**_ was settled as 500, _**Cap**_ for 4,000,000.

The _**Premine**_ is 15,000.

And leave other fields empty.Then you could input the above needed text as shown below,

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FCR5zzd7NfA9OxQmXXcH1%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1752c894-051b-4b5d-8286-1d86bdd0bff7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=87ccaf05&sv=2)

_Please note: you need to wait for 5 blocks confirmations for etching._

After the Rune is confirmed as valid, the etcher will get 15000E EVERYONE.LOVES.NATURE.FOREVER. Meantime, the others can mint Rune EVERYONE.LOVES.NATURE.FOREVER.

Following is the introduction for each parameter:

_**Rune:**_ Runes name, (currently you can ethi 13-26 characters long, can be separated by a middle dot ·, and the separator does not count towards the character limit).

_**Symbol (optional):**_ The symbol after the number of runes, which can be A-Z or empty. If empty, a general symbol ¤ will be used.

_**Mintable:**_ Toggle off to disable further minting. Runes are only premine upon creation.

_**Amount:**_ The Amount field contains the amount of runes each mint transaction receives.

_**Cap:**_ The number of times a rune may be minted is its cap. A mint is closed once the cap is reached.

_**Advanced options:**_ Set up premining, divisible figures, and the starting or ending block where minting is possible (optional).

_**Premine :**_ The etcher of a rune may optionally allocate to themselves units of the runes being etched. This allocation is called a premine.

_**Divisibility (optional):**_ A rune's divisibility is how finely it may be divided into its atomic units. Divisibility is expressed as the number of digits permissible after the decimal point in the amount of runes. A rune with divisibility 0 may not be divided. A unit of a rune with divisibility 1 may be divided into ten sub-units, a rune with divisibility 2 may be divided into a hundred, and so on.

_**Absolute Height:**_ The absolute block height (based on the current block height).

_**Relative Height：**_The range of relative block heights (based on the block of etching real).

_**Start Height：**_A mint is open starting in the block with the given start height.

_**End Height：**_A rune may not be minted in or after the block with the given end height.

Minded: You can find the Premine setting on the pop-up page after clicking _**Advanced Options**_.

[PreviousRunes](https://docs.unisat.io/runes)
[NextHow to Mint Runes?](https://docs.unisat.io/runes/how-to-mint-runes)

# Alkanes | UniSat

**What is Alkanes？**

Alkanes is a token-based smart contract metaprotocol built on the protorunes framework using the protorunes standard, designed to enable smart contract functionality through a combination of WebAssembly (WASM) and UTXO-based transactions.

**Key Features**

*   UTXO-Based Smart Contracts
    

Alkanes leverages Bitcoin’s UTXO model to deploy smart contracts, embedding WASM code through inscriptions similar to Ordinals for on-chain execution.

*   WASM-Driven with Storage Optimization
    

Contracts are written in Rust, compiled into gzip-compressed WASM binaries, and embedded in Bitcoin transactions to align with storage constraints.

*   Protorunes Framework
    

Built on the Protorunes standard, inheriting design patterns from Ordinals and Runes, using a witness envelope to deploy WASM files and enable contract interactions.

*   Metashrew Open-Source Indexer for Contract State Tracking
    

Integrates the open-source Metashrew indexer to track contract states, supporting real-time data access and validation on Bitcoin.

**UniSat Product Support for Alkanes**

*   UniSat Wallet
    
*   UniScan
    
*   UniSat UTXO Management Tool
    
*   UniSat Marketplace
    

?

Learn more: [https://alkanes.build/docs/developers/disclaimer](https://alkanes.build/docs/developers/disclaimer)

[NextHow to Trade Alkanes on UniSat Marketplace](https://docs.unisat.io/alkanes/how-to-trade-alkanes-on-unisat-marketplace)

# How to Mint Runes? | UniSat

Go to Mint option on page [https://unisat.io/runes/inscribe](https://unisat.io/runes/inscribe)
.

Or you could explore Rune information on [https://unisat.io/runes/list](https://unisat.io/runes/list)
 and Click ‘Mint Directly’ button if the rune can be mintable for more convenience.

You could input the _**Rune or Rune ID**_ as below.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fz482fDtRbiXaXfQuqapK%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D64f5a17e-2d65-4c8c-9e4e-73e4c7b70fdb&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f6509337&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FODmNseZuYgBrpa3nIwih%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1a78de5b-191b-4d71-82bb-e5188f2fb8d7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4d7fa101&sv=2)

You can input the number of _**Repet Mint**_ or use the slide bar for batch minting.

_**Let’s take the Rune: EVERYONE.LOVES.NATURE.FOREVER for example.**_

There will be 500E for one minting. If _**Repeat Mint**_\=53, the balance is 500\*53=26500E

EVERYONE.LOVES.NATURE.FOREVER after minting transaction was confirmed. At the same time, the _**Cap**_ of this Rune was reduced from 4,000,000 to 3,999,947.

After the transaction (including etching, minting, etc) has been confirmed on chain, you may refer to the following formula for the current total supply of Rune：

_**Supply=Premine+Amount\*Mints**_

1) If Premine=1000, the Rune is mintable and Amount=100, Mints=90, then Supply=1000+100\*90=10000;2）

2) If Premine=0, the Rune is mintable and Amount=100, Mints=90, then Supply=0+100\*90=9000;3）

3) If Premine=10000, the Rune is non-mintable, then Supply=10000+0\*0=10000;4）

4) If Premine=0, the Rune is non-mintable, then Supply=0+0\*0=10000.(This Rune is Cenotaph)

[NextHow to Trade Runes？](https://docs.unisat.io/runes/how-to-trade-runes)

# FAQ | UniSat

**UTXO Management Tool:** [https://unisat.io/utxo](https://unisat.io/utxo)

**Q: What is UTXO?**

Each UTXO (Unspent Transaction Output) represents a spendable balance in Bitcoin or Fractal.

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/faq#consolidate-faq)

**Consolidate FAQ**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

_Lower fee = more BTC in your pocket! Consolidating is optimal when network fees are <3 sats/vB!_

**Q: What are useless inscriptions? Will merging them affect my brc-20 assets?**

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fj80RMt4NIGdPO9BSMtQz%252F17.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D537ca0ab-76c6-4af2-9c01-0471760a46ec&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c8304050&sv=2)

There are currently two types: **brc-20 Mint inscriptions and used brc-20 Transfer inscriptions.**

These types of brc-20 inscriptions have no value and are not linked to your brc-20 asset holdings. Merging and spending them will not affect your brc-20 balance.

However, each inscription typically occupies 294–546 sats. If you have a large quantity of these types of useless inscriptions, they can take up a significant portion of your balance. Consolidating them when the fee rate is low can help you reclaim at least 60% of usable BTC.

**Q: Since useless inscriptions include brc-20 Transfer inscriptions, are minted but unused brc-20 Transfer inscriptions safe?**

Yes, they are safe. Valid and unused brc-20 Transfer inscriptions will not be classified as useless inscriptions and will appear in the "UTXO list".

**Q: Will consolidated useless inscription UTXOs become spendable BTC in the wallet?**

Yes. After consolidating, they usually exceed 600 sats and will appear as available balance in the wallet.

**Q: Why does consolidating useless inscriptions UTXOs consume high gas fees?**

Gas fee = fee rate × virtual transaction size. The more inputs a transaction has, the larger the size, and thus the higher the fee. We recommend merging when fees are relatively low to process.

**Q: Is there a service fee for consolidating useless inscription UTXOs? Will I earn points?**

You get three free **consolidations up to 3000 UTXOs each month,** effectively no charge. For consolidate with a service fee, corresponding UniSat Points will be awarded. More details [here](https://docs.unisat.io/unisat-services/guides-and-explanations/unisat-points-explained)
.

* * *

[](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/faq#unlock-utxos-under-all-utxos-tab-faq)

Unlock UTXOs under "All UTXOs" tab FAQ


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

_**📌 Unlock with care**_

_**UTXOs with brc-20, ordinals NFT , Alkanes or Runes assets are treated as BTC after unlocking — you may burn valuable assets if mistakenly select the wrong UTXO.**_

**Q: How do I unlock assets using the UTXO Management Tool?**

_Tips: Before unlocking, make sure the UTXOs’ assets are useless/unwanted to avoid losing anything valuable._

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Frkxk5YvagAoZmSF9RrCd%252Funlock%2520new.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2eb2b389-ce29-4015-ac43-a05992f658ec&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=76ce5468&sv=2)

**Q: Can unlocked inscription/Runes/Alkanes UTXOs be used directly as BTC in the UniSat wallet?**

Yes, and there are two cases:

*   If the UTXO is >600 sats, your available balance in wallet will update its amount after unlocking, and it can be used directly as BTC.
    
*   If the UTXO is <600 sats, your available balance won’t update. It cannot be directly selected in the wallet for sending. You must go to the UTXO Management tool https://unisat.io/utxo to send it. _(Detailed steps_ [_here_](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-unlock-lock-inscription-runes-alkanes-utxo-and-send-as-normal-btc-in-all-utxo-tab)
    _)_
    

**Q: Why do unlocked UTXOs get locked again after being used?**

If a UTXO contains assets that UniSat can recognize—such as inscriptions or runes, the system will require you to manually confirm and unlock it before each spend to ensure your assets remain secure.

**Q: Can unlocked inscription/Alkanes/Runes UTXOs be sent to other addresses such as exchanges' wallet addresses? Will they turn into available BTC?**

Yes, if you do not wish to keep these assets, you can send them anywhere. \*Whether they appear as available BTC on any platform depends on whether that platform recognizes and locks the asset. If not, they will show up as unavailable BTC.

**Q：How many UTXOs can I unlock or merge at once?**

You can unlock or merge up to 500 UTXOs at a time. We may improve this limit in future updates.

* * *

**Q: If I select UTXOs on the current page, then go to the next page, will my selections be saved?**

No. Currently, selection is only valid on the current page. If you have many UTXOs, please increase the number of items displayed per page at the bottom, and use the category filter in the top right to narrow your list.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fz2vf6jtQjmgr6cJeerY4%252F19.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D56c6210c-163c-4985-b7c8-012ac7f80418&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7ba8be17&sv=2)

* * *

**Q: Will unsupported small UTXOs be spent automatically in my UniSat wallet?**

If your address has unsupported protocol assets stored in UTXOs under 600 sats, you cannot spend them directly unless you manually select and send them via our UTXO Management tool https://unisat.io/utxo. Please operate with caution when doing so.

* * *

**Q: Why does it say "Not enough BTC UTXOs available for network fee payment" when splitting BTC?** This occurs when the user only has one BTC UTXO or selects all BTC UTXOs for splitting, leaving none to pay the network fee. Solution: Reserve enough BTC from the split amount to cover the fee.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FnVkJLHNzcCVDWGXKgQTo%252F18.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D796600e2-a509-49c5-ada4-ca6f4656f6a7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b06a46&sv=2)

* * *

**Q: Why does the UTXO quantity show as 0 when trying to split Runes or Alkanes?** If the UTXO quantity shows as 0 on the split interface, it means the current settings do not allow the UTXO to be split. This can happen due to the asset's decimal support, the maximum allowed decimal places, or your specific split configuration. Please refer to the examples below:

*   Example 1: The asset does not support decimals and must be split in whole numbers. Attempting to split 1 unit into 3 parts results in decimals, so splitting is not possible. Illustration:
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FNClwY5SqOKeC6YwkIkyY%252F99.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D89cc00cc-7c96-47f1-908e-dd6abccbe495&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=76c7b66b&sv=2)

*   Example 2: The asset supports 2 decimal places. Attempting to split 0.01 units into 2 parts exceeds the supported decimal precision, so splitting is not possible.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FSC0hYaZTRZtaT8uCtOUj%252F88.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2d7c7a8d-360c-4b5b-8682-0e9606a0d212&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=26bd170&sv=2)

*   Example 3: Alkanes assets support 8 decimal places by default. Attempting to split 0.00000001 units into 2 parts exceeds the 8-decimal limit, so splitting is not possible.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fkw5Zc1ys0C6iRlTsdiG1%252F77.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5e87f67b-1c97-4ec5-97de-c5170f3c5142&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=88af162b&sv=2)

# How to Mint Runes? | UniSat

    .

# CAT on Fractal | UniSat

The Covenant Attested Token (CAT) Protocol is a UTXO-based token system on Bitcoin, validated by miners using Bitcoin Script at Layer 1. It manages token minting and transfers via smart contracts called covenants.

Key features include no reliance on external indexers, ensuring security through Bitcoin's consensus; modularity, allowing integration with various decentralized applications like AMMs and lending; programmable minting rules controlled by smart contracts; cross-chain interoperability for trustless asset bridging; and support for Simplified Payment Verification (SPV), enabling light clients to independently verify token authenticity.

CAT protocol supports both fungible tokens (called [**CAT20**](https://catprotocol.org/cat20)
 standard) and non-fungible tokens (called [**CAT721**](https://catprotocol.org/cat721)
 standard). For more detail: [https://catprotocol.org/](https://catprotocol.org/)

[PreviousHow to Trade Runes？](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/runes-on-fractal/how-to-trade-runes)
[NextHow to send / receive CAT20?](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-send-receive-cat20)

# How to Etch Runes? | UniSat

You may visit [https://fractal.unisat.io/runes/inscribe](https://fractal.unisat.io/runes/inscribe)
 to get the page.

Input the parameters as needed.

_**For example**_：

The _**Rune**_ Name is everyone.loves.nature.forever,

_**Symbol**_ is E,

It is _**Mintable**_, and _**Amount**_ was settled as 500, _**Cap**_ for 4,000,000.

The _**Premine**_ is 15,000.

**With Logo** option, select whether to add a logo for Runes.

And leave other fields empty.Then you could input the above needed text as shown below,

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FGbnFRY19zfNEeydTRSiK%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4e901ae5-bd13-48c4-b085-273e2ac0f417&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ceb6caf2&sv=2)

_Please note: you need to wait for 5 blocks confirmations for etching._

After the Rune is confirmed as valid, the etcher will get 15000E everyone.loves.nature.forever. Meantime, the others can mint Rune everyone.loves.nature.forever.

Following is the introduction for each parameter:

_**Rune:**_ Runes name, (currently you can etch 13-26 characters long, can be separated by a middle dot ·, and the separator does not count towards the character limit).

_**Symbol (optional):**_ The symbol after the number of runes, which can be A-Z or empty. If empty, a general symbol ¤ will be used.

_**Mintable:**_ Toggle off to disable further minting. Runes are only premine upon creation.

_**Amount:**_ The Amount field contains the amount of runes each mint transaction receives.

_**Cap:**_ The number of times a rune may be minted is its cap. A mint is closed once the cap is reached.

_**Advanced options:**_ Set up premining, divisible figures, and the starting or ending block where minting is possible (optional).

_**Premine :**_ The etcher of a rune may optionally allocate to themselves units of the runes being etched. This allocation is called a premine.

_**Divisibility (optional):**_ A rune's divisibility is how finely it may be divided into its atomic units. Divisibility is expressed as the number of digits permissible after the decimal point in the amount of runes. A rune with divisibility 0 may not be divided. A unit of a rune with divisibility 1 may be divided into ten sub-units, a rune with divisibility 2 may be divided into a hundred, and so on.

_**Absolute Height:**_ The absolute block height (based on the current block height).

_**Relative Height：**_The range of relative block heights (based on the block of etching real).

_**Start Height：**_A mint is open starting in the block with the given start height.

_**End Height：**_A rune may not be minted in or after the block with the given end height.

[PreviousRunes on Fractal](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/runes-on-fractal)
[NextHow to Mint Runes?](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/runes-on-fractal/how-to-mint-runes)

# How to Participate in BTC Staking on Babylon Using UniSat Wallet | UniSat

We support you in using UniSat Extension Wallet to participate in Babylon’s BTC staking activities, offering a seamless Bitcoin staking experience. This guide is for reference only. Participation in staking is at the user’s own discretion and responsibility.

**Step 1: Prepare Your UniSat Wallet**

Please ensure that your UniSat Extension Wallet or UniSat App Wallet is updated to the latest version. Click this link to download or update: [https://unisat.io/download](https://unisat.io/download)

**Step 2: Access the Babylon DApp**

*   Switch your network to Bitcoin Mainnet.
    
*   Open the wallet menu at the bottom, click Discover (DApp Center), find Babylon, and click to enter.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FD8PQsKARKUmx9Oo7nlnm%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dcb5b0457-0e0c-4489-bf98-99e6f618e81b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d1b4500b&sv=2)

**Step 3: Participate in Babylon Phase 2 Staking**

1.  After entering the Babylon Bitcoin Staking interface, you will see the **Babylon Bitcoin Staking Phase 2** page. Click the **Go to Babylon** button to proceed to the staking page.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FFsHiwFmy0egTREf4QSLr%252F2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D420bd808-5108-4c77-be04-54c4d5c99a7f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ce9c3e8e&sv=2)

1.  Click the **Connect Wallet** button in the top right corner. You will be prompted to connect your Bitcoin wallet address and your Babylon chain wallet address. Please select your **UniSat Wallet** for both.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FScCKSEWSuABQ2CfUBY58%252F3.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1fa0ba11-9e71-4314-922d-a5f2e3546c90&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4862c7b9&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F1lRAZEJUaSnfUYeJjxyZ%252F4.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db170cbd1-fd8e-4f83-abc6-b7ce47a8a4bc&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=76960ec9&sv=2)

1.  Choose the staking pool you want to participate in, enter the amount of BTC you wish to stake, confirm the amount, and click **Preview** to sign and complete the transaction.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F0i4Ct8VfVoBagMHgntgA%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D329872a8-dbbb-45bc-8165-1d3cf7943a1b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b64fd038&sv=2)

1.  Once your staking is complete, you can view your staking history in the **Staking History** section.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FvoYf2xBtKeDOr5PsRggj%252F6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2dfd9469-8e0e-4b4f-b23b-b394119b5267&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f8c60069&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/community/events/babylon-staking-activity/how-to-participate-in-btc-staking-on-babylon-using-unisat-wallet#tips)

Tips：

*   If the Babylon DApp entry is not showing in your UniSat wallet, please ensure your wallet is updated to the latest version.
    
*   If you encounter any technical issues, we recommend contacting Babylon’s official support at https://discord.com/invite/babylonglobal or reaching out to us via our Discord: http://discord.gg/unisat
    
*   Please make sure you fully understand the associated risks and terms before participating in staking.
    

**For more information on Babylon BTC staking, please refer to their official documentation:** [https://docs.babylonlabs.io/guides/overview/bitcoin\_staking/](https://docs.babylonlabs.io/guides/overview/bitcoin_staking/)

# How to unlock/lock inscription/Runes/Alkanes/ utxo and send as normal BTC in All UTXO Tab | UniSat

The **Lock** function in UniSat UTXO Management Tool allows you to prevent specific UTXOs from being accidentally used in transactions. The **Unlock** function lets you reverse this, making the UTXOs available again for normal operations.

Locking is helpful for protecting assets, reserving UTXOs for specific use cases, or managing wallet behavior.

UniSat UTXO Management Tool: [https://unisat.io/utxo](https://unisat.io/utxo)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fbp2IXgTh3Hjj02XYhuY2%252Flock.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd4f1aaa5-350e-46f9-9ace-c4066b6dd057&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6369c2d3&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-unlock-lock-inscription-runes-alkanes-utxo-and-send-as-normal-btc-in-all-utxo-tab#how-to-unlock-inscription-runes-alkanes-utxo-and-send-as-normal-btc-in-all-utxo-tab)

How to unlock inscription/runes/Alkanes/ utxo and send as normal BTC in All UTXO Tab?

_**📌 Unlock with care**_

_**UTXOs with brc-20, ordinals NFT, Alkanes or Runes assets are treated as BTC after unlocking — you may burn valuable assets if mistakenly select the wrong UTXO.**_

**📌 First please be 100% sure you don't want to keep these assets "inscriptions, Runes, Alkanes" at all, because once you unlock and send, you will lose these assets.**

Here, we use inscription as an example (The process for Ordinals, Runes, Alkanes, and BTC is similar, with slight differences based on asset type. Please refer to the specific interface for each asset.)

1\. select the related utxos and then unlock.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FLNoXddIpEEwt2cqnpOuu%252F31.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8dad628f-7f57-4ce6-a20b-a3429dc23f8b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3726baba&sv=2)

2\. You need to confirm and sign in wallet to finish unlocking.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FF8QaGJWa7Cx5P0u15FlF%252F32.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd9d40683-d2ca-4273-8a1c-76a3bd5a0561&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f87bfd80&sv=2)

3\. Then you could see these two utxos being unlocked. Then select them and click Send.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FLimYHDwffMw0zxcrpJLn%252F33.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D774e66a6-c3f8-4f26-87ea-b029722c10cd&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b1f6271&sv=2)

1.  There is a Notice that pops out because these utxos are less than 600 sats, to protect your assets, we need you to confirm again, if be sure, you could click Next to continue.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FvD0v1KLU6nCETzUf6eCQ%252F34.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dac1d0d3d-23fe-4f86-8c51-66df05ac65f7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c268e1e0&sv=2)

1.  Then you could enter Recipient and Amount, custom fee rate and confirm. In Sign page of wallet, you could see it lists these two utxos as Inputs.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FIa3tg6uCPlSGrP0OMMeo%252F35.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4cc8414c-63ad-41a8-92aa-75a05c62b8b0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=17b0a0b5&sv=2)

*   **Note:**
    
    *   After manually unlocking and spending a UTXO with assets, it needs to be unlocked again before the next spend.
        
    *   UTXOs with less than 600 sats, once unlocked, can only be merged or sent through the UTXO Management Tool. The wallet will not automatically select UTXOs below 600 sats for spending.
        
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/utxo-management/how-to-unlock-lock-inscription-runes-alkanes-utxo-and-send-as-normal-btc-in-all-utxo-tab#how-to-lock-inscription-runes-alkanes-utxo-and-send-as-normal-btc-in-all-utxo-tab)

How to lock inscription/Runes/Alkanes/ utxo and send as normal BTC in All UTXO Tab?

Here, we use Alkanes assets as an example (The process for Ordinals, Runes, Alkanes, and BTC is similar, with slight differences based on asset type. Please refer to the specific interface for each asset.)

**⚠ Always double-check before pressing that confirm button!**

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FuOFUg4E0DVf5j6cO7iEp%252Flock.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De71bf49d-4ab7-4406-ae4a-6912840c2c89&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3980fcb&sv=2)

# Liquidity providers (LPs) | UniSat

When you provide liquidity, you will receive LP tokens in return. These tokens represent your share of the liquidity pool. Keep these tokens safe, as they are essential for withdrawing your liquidity and claiming your share of the fees.

Things to keep in mind as a Liquidity Provider:

1.  **Impermanent Loss:** When you provide liquidity, you expose yourself to the risk of impermanent loss, which occurs when the value of one of the tokens in the pool changes significantly compared to when you added liquidity.
    
2.  **Fees and Rewards:** As an LP, you earn a share of the trading fees paid by users. Keep an eye on the rewards and fees you are earning.
    
3.  **Regular Monitoring:** Check your LP position periodically to ensure it remains balanced. You may need to add or withdraw tokens to maintain the desired balance.
    
4.  **Withdrawal:** When you're ready to withdraw your liquidity, use your LP tokens to remove your assets from the pool.
    
5.  **Risk Management:** Understand the risks associated with providing liquidity, and only invest what you can afford to lose. Diversify your investments and do your own research before choosing a liquidity pool.
    

[PreviousWhat Is an Automated Market Maker?](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker)
[NextTestnet guide](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/testnet-guide)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Understanding Sub-1 sat/vB Bitcoin Transactions | UniSat

**The 1 sat/vB Minimum Standard**

Bitcoin fees are measured in satoshis per virtual byte (sat/vB). Most network nodes enforce a default relay policy requiring ≥1 sat/vB to:

1.  Ensure miner incentives
    
2.  Discourage transaction spam
    
3.  Maintain efficient mempool operation
    

**How Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions Function**

*   Not publicly relayed: Ignored by standard nodes; excluded from public mempools.
    
*   Confirmation requirements:
    
    *   Direct submission to miners, _or_
        
    *   Private relay services (e.g., Slipstream).
        
    
*   Unpredictable inclusion: Miners rarely prioritize these. Confirmation occurs only during low congestion _if_ miners accept sub-1 sat policies.
    

[PreviousSingle-Step Transfer](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/single-step-transfer)
[NextWhat Happens When Bitcoin Fee Rates Drop Below 1 sat/vB?](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-when-bitcoin-fee-rates-drop-below-1-sat-vb)

# What Is an Automated Market Maker? | UniSat

brc20-swap implements the functionality of an automated market maker (AMM). This is the underlying technology that powers most decentralized exchanges (DEXs). You don’t need to have a counterparty (another trader) on the other side to make a trade. Instead, you interact with a liquidity pool by exchanging for a price calculated by a math formula.

brc20-swap specifically implements the **x \* y = k** formula, where **x** is the amount of one token in the liquidity pool, and **y** is the amount of the other. In this formula, **k** is a fixed constant, meaning the pool’s total liquidity always has to remain the same.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker#slippage)

Slippage


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

Slippage occurs when the actual price you get for a trade is different from the expected or quoted price. It often happens in situations of high market volatility or low liquidity. If you want to buy or sell an asset at a specific price, but the market conditions change before your trade is executed, you might end up with a slightly different price than you anticipated. Slippage can result in a higher or lower cost for your trade than you initially planned.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker#impermanent-loss)

Impermanent loss


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

Impermanent loss is a term used in liquidity provision. When you provide liquidity to a pool by depositing two different assets, the value of your assets can change over time due to price fluctuations. Impermanent loss occurs when the value of your assets in the pool is less than if you had simply held those assets without providing liquidity. It's "impermanent" because the loss can decrease or disappear as the prices of the assets change.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker#price-impact)

Price impact


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

Price impact refers to the effect a large trade has on the price of an asset in a market. When someone buys or sells a significant amount of an asset, it can cause the price to move in the direction of the trade due to the imbalance in supply and demand. The larger the trade relative to the overall liquidity in the market, the greater the price impact. Price impact can lead to higher or lower prices depending on whether it's a buy or sell order.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker#service-fee)

Service fee


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

Each swap incurs a 0.3% transaction fee, of which 1/6 goes to the platform as fees, and the remaining portion is received by LPs.

LP fees are accrued inside the pool. They don't need to be claimed.

LP tokens represent your share of assets in the pool. As fees accumulate in the pool, the amount of brc-20 assets backing your LP tokens will grow automatically. Just keep in mind, impermanent loss can affect your profitability.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker#rollup-fee)

Rollup fee


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

brc20-swap is able to reduce bitcoin network fees significantly. The brc20-swap sequencer bundles transactions and submits them to the Bitcoin network. brc20-swap charges a fee in SATS (brc-20) to cover Bitcoin network fees.

[Previousbrc20-swap Introduction](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction)
[NextLiquidity providers (LPs)](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/liquidity-providers-lps)

# FAQ | UniSat

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/alkanes/faq#id-1.-how-do-i-import-other-wallets-into-unisat)

1\. How do I import other wallets into UniSat?

We recommend creating a new UniSat wallet and sending your Alkanes assets to this new wallet.

❌ Directly importing your mnemonic or private key is not advised. Doing so may expose your assets to risk if your key is leaked or stolen during the process.

* * *

**2\. How do I create a new Alkanes wallet in UniSat?**

First, make sure your UniSat Wallet is updated to the latest version or download it [here](https://unisat.io/download)

*   On the wallet homepage, tap the **HD Wallet** icon in the top-left corner to access wallet management.
    
*   Click the **“+”** button to create a new wallet.
    

When creating a new wallet, you can choose from **four address types** — **all are fully compatible with Alkanes.** Select the one that suits your preferences; you can switch later if needed.

_Important: Be sure to securely back up your mnemonic phrase — this is essential for future recovery._

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FYtiRgG63CtvkqeLbRzIl%252F22.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D47b01d02-f3ce-427a-b706-c3d1123998e4&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cb8050d8&sv=2)

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/alkanes/faq#id-3.-do-i-need-to-care-about-address-type-when-sending-or-receiving-alkanes-in-unisat)

3\. **Do I need to care about address type when sending or receiving Alkanes in UniSat?**

*   Sending to UniSat wallet: No. UniSat supports Alkanes across all address types.
    
*   Receiving in UniSat wallet: No. UniSat wallet supports Alkanes across all address types
    
*   Sending from UniSat Wallet to other wallets: yes. Because other wallets may be double-address wallets that only support Alkanes on specific address types. - Please refer to target wallets for instructions on which address you should send your Alkanes to. For example, only bc1p address type supports Alkanes on Oyl Wallet. When sending to Oyl wallet, please send to bc1p.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/alkanes/faq#id-4.-can-i-batch-send-alkanes-assets-to-multiple-wallets-through-idclub-using-unisat-wallet)

4\. **Can I batch-send Alkanes assets to multiple wallets through idclub using unisat wallet??**

Yes, you can batch-send Alkanes via UniSat.

⚠️ However, the number of assets you can send in one batch is limited by OP\_RETURN data size.  

If your batch exceeds the limit, you will receive a pop-up warning message.

* * *
