# Simple Bridge | UniSat

Simple Bridge, developed by UniSat, is a small service designed to securely and efficiently connect assets from different protocols to PizzaSwap. By integrating the latest cryptographic algorithms, Simple Bridge enhances the security and performance of cross-chain asset transfers, bringing innovation to the blockchain ecosystem.

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/simple-bridge#key-features)

Key Features:

*   **Multisig with Anonymous Validators:** Simple Bridge secures transactions using a multi-signature system distributed across anonymous validator nodes. Each transaction is signed randomly by a subset of these nodes, increasing fault tolerance and making it harder for attackers to compromise the bridge.
    
*   **End-to-End Encrypted Communication:** All transaction data is transmitted using strong end-to-end encryption. Even if the data is intercepted, it cannot be deciphered—ensuring users' funds and information remain secure at all times.
    
*   **Distributed Service Architecture:** The service architecture of Simple Bridge is designed to be distributed, exposing only necessary nodes and minimizing potential security risks. This design makes the system more robust while improving overall operational efficiency.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/simple-bridge#supported-assets)

Supported Assets

*   At launch, Simple Bridge supports the following assets:sBTC, sORDI, sSATS, sQUAQ, sOSHI, sPEPE, sTRAC, sMEME, sRATS, sPIZZA
    
*   All bridged assets carry the **s-** prefix, signifying their status as cross-chain assets transferred via Simple Bridge.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/simple-bridge#naming-conventions)

Naming Conventions

To maintain consistency and ensure easy identification, Simple Bridge follows a specific naming convention for bridged assets:

*   Assets are prefixed with s-, indicating they are bridged through Simple Bridge.
    
*   For assets whose names are fewer than six characters, underscores ("\_") are used as padding to maintain consistency. For instance:
    
    *   sBTC is represented as sBTC\_\_\_000
        
    

This naming system ensures that all bridged assets meet a uniform format, making them easier to identify and manage.

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/simple-bridge#bridge-fees)

Bridge Fees

Using Simple Bridge incurs the following fees:

*   **Deposit Fee**: 0.00003 BTC
    
*   **Withdrawal Fee**: 0.25 FB
    

Simple Bridge will become an important tool for secure and efficient cross-chain transfers on Fractal Bitcoin, offering unmatched security, scalability, and ease of use. Backed by the expertise of the UniSat team, it provides a solid foundation for innovation and applications on Fractal Bitcoin.

[PreviousTransfer brc-20 in UniSat Wallet (2023)](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023)
[NextHow to use the Simple Bridge](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/simple-bridge/how-to-use-the-simple-bridge)

# What Happens When Bitcoin Fee Rates Drop Below 1 sat/vB? | UniSat

Bitcoin transaction fees are measured in **satoshis per virtual byte (sat/vB)**. This unit helps miners prioritize transactions when adding blocks to the blockchain. Bitcoin's **default relay policy** (followed by most nodes) requires a minimum fee rate of **1 sat/vB** for a transaction to be relayed across the network. This policy exists to:

1.  Provide a minimum economic incentive for miners to include transactions.
    
2.  Prevent spam by making it costly to flood the network.
    
3.  Maintain efficient network operation by limiting mempool bloat.
    

Transactions paying **less than 1 sat/vB** (sub-1 sat/vB) are considered **non-standard** under this default policy. This means:

However, as the ecosystem evolves there may be some demand for sub-1 sat/vB transactions and more occasions where the miner may accept these transactions such as when the mempool cleared recently.

So how do these sub-1 sat/vB transactions work?

* * *

**⏳ When Can Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions Be Confirmed?**

*   **Not Relayed:** They are **not broadcast or relayed** by nodes enforcing the default policy. They will **not enter the public mempool**.
    
*   **Confirmation only possible** if:
    
    1.  The transaction is **submitted directly to a miner** (bypassing the public peer-to-peer network), _or_
        
    2.  The transaction is submitted via a **private relay service** (like Slipstream used by some pools) that accepts sub-1 sat/vB rates, _or_
        
    
*   **Not Guaranteed:** Even if directly submitted to a miner or pool, **inclusion is never guaranteed**.
    

Miners prioritize transactions based on their own fee thresholds and strategies. Sub-1 sat/vB transactions are the lowest priority and will only be mined when there is plenty of unused block space and the individual miner or mining pool **explicitly chooses** to accept and mine sub-1 sat/vB transactions using custom mempool policies.

* * *

**💡 Potential Benefits of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions**

*   **Lower Costs:** _If confirmed_, they enable cheaper transactions, potentially benefiting low-value transfers or microtransactions. (It wouldn’t make sense if you want send $1 worth of BTC but have to spend $5 on gas right)
    
*   **Reduced Minting Costs:** Protocols relying heavily on on-chain transactions for operations like minting (e.g., Runes, Ordinals, BRC-20 tokens) could see significant cost reductions. More UNCOMMON•GOODS minted at -1sats/vb?
    

* * *

**⚠️ Downsides and Network Risks**

*   **Minimal Impact on Miner Revenue (Direct):** We think the direct impact on overall miner revenue is negligible, as sub-1 sat/vB transactions represent a tiny fraction of fees paid, especially compared to block rewards. However, widespread adoption _could_ exert downward pressure on fee rates.
    
*   Increased Spam Transactions: Lowering the _effective_ cost barrier significantly makes it cheaper for attackers to flood the network with spam or dust transactions (very small outputs), potentially disrupting normal operation.
    
*   UTXO **Proliferation**: Small transactions often create many unspent outputs (UTXOs), which increases the load on indexing services and node storage.
    
*   Mempool Strain: If nodes allow too many low-fee transactions, mempools may swell. This increases memory requirements for nodes, slows down mempool synchronization.
    

[PreviousUnderstanding Sub-1 sat/vB Bitcoin Transactions](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions)
[NextThe Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions)

Last updated 1 month ago

# Single-Step Transfer | UniSat

**What is Single-Step Transfer?**

Simply put, Single-Step Transfer combines what used to be a two-step process — inscribing a transfer and sending it — into a single, seamless action.

❌ Inscribe transfer inscription > send brc-20

✅ Send brc-20 in ONE STEP!

* * *

**Simplified Transfer Process**

Previously, if you wanted to transfer brc-20 assets (e.g., 100 ORDI) from Address A to Address B:

*   You had to inscribe a transfer, creating a Transfer inscription that locks part of Address A’s available balance into a transferable balance.
    
*   Only after that, you could send your ORDI to Address B, enabling B to receive the assets.
    

Two steps, two transactions, higher fees.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F9S4WXpaJBvgC1UkVofVp%252Fimage%2520%2823%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D07ef6169-aaeb-4c02-b558-7748bbc6f83d&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=baf9f290&sv=2)

* * *

**Now with Single-Step Transfer:**

On the Send page, simply enter the recipient's address and the amount you want to send — just like sending FB.

One step, one transaction — fast and simple!

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FAT98QvyLI52rQdQfin72%252Fimage%2520%2824%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc23651df-7b47-4ed6-86d0-cce7e36489db&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ec538fc7&sv=2)

* * *

**Why It Matters:**

*   Cuts Costs: By combining two transactions into one, you pay significantly lower fees, making brc-20 transfers more affordable.
    
*   Saves Time: Skip the tedious step of creating a Transfer inscription. Enter the recipient’s address, set the amount, and send—done!
    
*   Streamlines Experience: Simplifies the process when trading brc-20 in a DEX like PizzaSwap or in marketplace.
    
*   Batch transfers: Future updates will allow transferring to up to 1,000 addresses in a single transaction with multiple single-step transfers.
    

* * *

**New Features with Single-Step Transfer:**

**🔸 Signed Mint Inscriptions:** Inscribe mint operations using the Single-Step Transfer method - directly inscribe into OP\_RETURN to prevent creating useless UTXOs at your address.

**🔸 Batch inscribing for Single-Step Transfers (deploy/mint/traditional transfers remain individual)**, and allows spending from UTXOs carrying useless inscriptions to reduce waste and improve efficiency.

* * *

**Why Launch on Fractal Testnet First?**

As a Bitcoin-native extension, Fractal resembles Bitcoin closely in its design and adopts the Bitcoin core code, making it the perfect testing ground for upgrades before Bitcoin mainnet deployment.

Our approach to upgrades has always been to remain optimistic about innovations while maintaining steady, careful rollouts to safeguard network integrity and protect user interests. We anticipate that real-world usage on Fractal will help developers to harness the real potential of these brc-20 upgrades.

Fractal’s Highlights:

*   30-second block time — 20× faster than Bitcoin — enabling quicker confirmations and much shorter transaction wait times.
    
*   Perfect for fast-trading scenarios, such as swapping brc-20 assets on PizzaSwap!
    

* * *

**What's Next?**

*   brc-20 Single-Step Transfer now live on Frdctal Mainnet
    
*   Support will gradually roll out across UniSat's Inscribe, Wallet, Explorer, and Marketplace, as well as on PizzaSwap.
    
*   We will closely monitor its performance on Fractal network and continue to advocate for its deployment on Bitcoin mainnet.
    

[PreviousFractal Service Links](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/fractal-service-links)
[NextUnderstanding Sub-1 sat/vB Bitcoin Transactions](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions)

# Technical Q&A | UniSat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#what-are-the-considerations-for-using-brc20-sats-as-l2-gas)

What are the considerations for using brc20-sats as L2 gas?

* * *

Using brc20-sats as L2 gas has several considerations:

1.  **Wide Distribution**: brc20-sats are the most widely distributed brc20 assets to date, with the largest number of holding addresses. This wide distribution makes it a practical choice.
    
2.  **Fine-Grained Value Measurement**: brc20-sats have a relatively small unit, allowing for precise value measurement. This is especially valuable in situations where small amounts of value need to be calculated and transferred.
    
3.  **Consistency with Layer 1**: Using brc20-sats as L2 gas maintains relative consistency with the use of Bitcoin-sats on the Layer 1 network. This consistency can simplify the user experience and provide continuity in value representation between the two layers.
    

In summary, using brc20-sats as L2 gas offers practicality due to their widespread distribution, fine-grained value measurement, and consistency with Bitcoin-sats used on Layer 1. These factors contribute to a seamless and user-friendly experience in both L1 & L2 of the network.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#will-people-receive-rewards-for-providing-liquidity)

**Will people receive rewards for providing liquidity?**

* * *

Yes.

UniSat offers two types of rewards to users who provide liquidity:

1.  Service Fee: Liquidity providers receive a portion of the swap service fee as a reward for their participation.
    
2.  Staking of LP Tokens: UniSat provides a farming mechanism, enabling third-party developers to establish their staking models. This allows for additional rewards to be offered for specific swap pairs.
    

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#can-you-explain-how-brc-20-modules-work-and-why-should-we-care)

**Can you explain how brc-20 modules work and why should we care?**

* * *

(this is technical, skip if you are not interested in development)

Anyone can implement their own modules, which is permissionless, much like UniSat has done with the brc20-swap module. All newly created modules start in 'black module' mode by default, meaning that all indexers treat them as blackboxes, not recognizing their contents.

To provide services to their users, module providers must independently index data within their modules. All activities within these modules remain hidden from the external world and have no impact on the existing brc-20 ecosystem.

Once the main indexers (Alex, Domo, Hiro, OKX, UniSat) are ready to recognize brc20-swap operations and are satisfied with its performance (let's assume that they are happy with it), the brc20-swap module has the opportunity to be 'accepted' and become a part of the brc-20 as one 'white module'.

Looking ahead, the core protocol will remain stable and straightforward. Many modules supporting various protocols, blockchains, and domains will be introduced. Some of these modules will gain acceptance from the main indexers.

This approach allows brc-20 to remain highly adaptable, permissionless (meaning anyone can create modules), decentralized (as indexers can choose which modules to support), and sustainable (modules are isolated without interfering with each other), all while keeping the core protocol simple and stable.

Numerous modules are currently in development (Sep. 2023), aiming to support different protocols, blockchains, and domains. brc-20 is showcasing its robustness and vitality through its inherent simplicity.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#i-heard-withdrawal-is-restricted-when-in-the-black-module-can-you-describe-the-details)

**I heard withdrawal is restricted when in the 'black module', can you describe the details?**

* * *

In the 'black module' state, the main indexers lack detailed information about the module. Allowing direct withdrawals in this state would result in varying states across different indexers, potentially causing chaos in the entire system. This is why direct withdrawal is not an option for 'black modules.'

Nevertheless, there are multiple workarounds available. The most straightforward approach is to utilize existing marketplaces, where users can trade in-module assets (L2 assets) for classic brc-20 assets (L1 assets).

However, we offer a simpler solution: when a user requests a withdrawal, they simply submit the withdrawal request. If there is someone depositing assets, the deposit and withdrawal processes will automatically and atomically exchange, ensuring a smooth and atomic deposit/withdrawal happening at the same time.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#more-details-about-the-sequencer-and-rollup)

**More details about the sequencer and rollup?**

* * *

To address the congestion challenges on the Bitcoin mainnet, UniSat has developed a sequencer capable of rolling up thousands of swap operations, including adding liquidity, removing liquidity, and swapping assets. The resulting rollup inscription is then submitted to the Bitcoin mainnet.

What makes this sequencer truly remarkable is its versatility. It's designed in a way that allows it not only to roll up swap operations but also to be extended to support various advanced operations in the future.

It's quite encouraging that we now have a comprehensive Layer 2 solution with Ordinals on Bitcoin, all achieved elegantly. This achievement highlights the inherent strength of brc-20 and showcases its potential for further innovation.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a#how-do-you-make-sure-that-it-is-accepted-by-all-indexers-and-that-there-is-complete-consensus-if-som)

**How do you make sure that it is accepted by all indexers and that there is complete consensus? If some indexers have not accepted, how to deal with it?**

* * *

To provide a more feature-rich experience, the current main indexers may show interest in implementing useful and highly reliable modules. This becomes even more likely when the source code is available for thorough review and reference.

In the ever-evolving ecosystem, An indexer is expected to communicate well with others and make decisions thoughtfully about supporting different modules. If it remains stagnant may find itself outperformed by newer counterparts and risk losing support over the long term.

Ideally, having the support of all indexers for a module would be fantastic. However, it's essential to acknowledge that in reality, there might be cases where most indexers adopt a module while the rest have reservations and choose to step back without following. In such scenarios, the indexer is risking being orphaned, which reflects the reality well.

The governance of brc-20 is a journey that stretches into the future. UniSat holds immense respect for other participants in this field and wholeheartedly supports the development of a robust and ever-evolving ecosystem.

[PreviousTestnet guide](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/testnet-guide)
[NextModules, withdrawals, and decentralization of brc-20](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Modules, withdrawals, and decentralization of brc-20 | UniSat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20#brc20-swap-as-a-module)

brc20-swap as a module

The modular extension of brc-20 is achieved in the following way:

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FnaAmE35SC7HTFHcqGXfP%252Fp1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dab3a1c41-1c90-4354-8c1c-23b082b8fd04&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=697c8310&sv=2)

In the diagram above, we can see that each extension module exists independently of the core brc-20 protocol.

This approach has several advantages for brc-20:

1.  **Permissionless Development**: Developing new modules for brc-20 is a permissionless process, and new modules start as black modules, being naturally separated from the core protocol and other modules.
    
2.  **Isolated Execution**: If there are issues with the implementation of any module, the isolation between black modules ensures it does not affect the operation of the core protocol and other modules.
    
3.  **Consensus Upgrading**: When the majority of indexers recognize and implement indexing for a specific module, it can transition to a white module, becoming a natural part of the brc-20 protocol.
    

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20#black-module-module-as-a-blackbox-non-withdrawable)

Black Module: Module as a blackbox (non-withdrawable)

However, the modular extension model has a drawback when a module is a black module, as it can not achieve free withdrawals, as illustrated in the image below:

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F6GTWDeIvLHtYvuK8TbHG%252Fp2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5732dc52-21db-4790-befa-14c297586a18&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e5809f9d&sv=2)

This is because when a module operates as a black module, it means that major indexers do not acknowledge the reliability of its operation. To them, this module is a black box, and its internal state is not recognized as valid brc-20 state. Therefore, the calculated balances are not considered valid brc-20 balances, and assets within this module cannot be freely withdrawn to brc-20.

Imagine if black modules could arbitrarily extend the brc-20 protocol. Developers could create modules like brc20-100x, which would allow users to receive a hundred times the deposited amount. For instance, if you deposited 5 ordi, you would receive 500 ordi. Such unrestricted inflation is unacceptable for the core brc-20 protocol.

Hence, for responsible indexers, all unverified black modules and their internal mechanisms are deemed untrustworthy.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20#white-module-consensus-upgrading)

White Module: Consensus Upgrading

The behavior of a module gradually becomes reliable when it is understood and executed in the real world. This gradual acceptance by more indexers eventually allows its behavior to be considered reliable and transforms it into a white module, becoming part of the upgraded consensus.

Transitioning to a white module means that the balances it calculates are widely recognized and can be securely interacted with the brc-20 main network. In other words, users can safely, freely, and at any time withdraw to the brc-20 main network (as shown in the image below).

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FwhE81YF1oFY8t85n9Ba8%252Fp3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7e7fc7f3-8065-4146-96c1-5ecd6a2964aa&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=51aba699&sv=2)

The fundamental difference between black module and white module, when compared, is whether they allow users to withdraw freely.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20#withdraw-assets-from-black-module)

Withdraw assets from black module

A system that only allows deposits but not withdrawals is unacceptable from a functional perspective.

To address this issue, we conducted in-depth research and were inspired by the matching mechanism in UniSat Marketplace's activities. We dynamically matched User A's deposit request with User B's withdrawal request, allowing the system to use deposit transactions to fulfill withdrawal needs.

The process is illustrated in the image below:

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FL6BIUQsJw4nyRni7W96i%252Fp4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0df0a9eb-c760-4366-a190-ea1ec0197bda&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=928b7abf&sv=2)

In the image above, User A initiates a withdrawal request of 80 ordi, while User B initiates a deposit request of 20 ordi.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FYOokVzBk8kLfNIHmAZYn%252Fp5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D361307ba-8282-411f-9f3a-9988ee4d2130&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=79ca874b&sv=2)

At this point, the system dynamically matches their needs, using User B's 20 ordi deposit to fulfill part of User A's withdrawal request (20/80). User B can continue to wait for other users' deposits to achieve more withdrawals.

When brc20-swap operates as a black module, **withdrawal requests can only be satisfied when users deposit assets from outside the module**. In other words, if an asset lacks sufficient deposit requests, the corresponding withdrawal requests will be challenging to fulfill promptly, significantly impacting the user experience.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/modules-withdrawals-and-decentralization-of-brc-20#decentralization-a-pragmatic-process)

Decentralization: a pragmatic process

During the early stages of brc-20 development, UniSat provided users with a complete indexing service for transaction and balance inquiries, which led to general centralization concerns:

*   If the system were to rely on UniSat for rule interpretation and execution, would UniSat possess a form of centralized authority, potentially leading to the brc-20 protocol being controlled by a single development team?
    

Regarding this question, there are three levels of observation:

1.  **Non-mandatory**: Indexing primarily involves the analysis and organization of on-chain data to make it more comprehensible to humans, and it depends on the predefined rules of the protocol. It operates on immutable data and has no chance to alter past transactions. UniSat's code for indexing and execution is open source, allowing anyone to inspect it to ensure it aligns with the brc-20 rules.
    
2.  **Competition and Robustness**: With the emergence of multiple indexing service providers, there is increased reliability through redundancy. Errors in results from one index provider are more likely to be identified when compared to others. If any single indexer were to cease operations, it wouldn't impact the overall results. In fact, even if all indexers were to stop functioning, brc-20 could continue operating robustly and users would still have the ability to DEPLOY / MINT / TRANSFER as usual. No critical operations rely on indexing support.
    
3.  **Governance and Consensus**: Given the participation of multiple indexers in the system, the module mechanism being implemented allows different service providers to effectively learn how to govern and extend the brc-20 protocol in a managable way.
    

When implementing the UniSat brc-20 indexer, we did not anticipate that other service providers would follow suit. Subsequently, different indexing providers independently began offering indexing services. This process was spontaneous and permissionless, making it a healthy evolution overall. The transition of brc20-swap from a black module to a white module, if successful, will be able to mirror this process.

Within the module architecture, the barrier for service providers to index data is further lowered. In the past, indexers needed to accurately process all network transactions to be considered a valid indexer. Now, indexing data only within their own black module is sufficient to commence providing indexing services, which requires significantly less effort compared to handling all brc-20 data on the network.

Therefore, with the widespread adoption of modules, it's reasonable to expect a substantial increase in the number of indexes, and some services may gradually evolve to offer comprehensive data indexing.

[PreviousTechnical Q&A](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/technical-q-and-a)
[Nextbrc-20 Swap and PizzaSwap Development](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc-20-swap-and-pizzaswap-development)

Last updated 1 year ago

# The Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions | UniSat

While sub-1 sat/vB transactions might seem appealing due to lower fees, they introduce serious risks that every user should understand before using them. These risks can lead to stuck transactions, financial losses, and poor user experience.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-1-stuck-transactions)

#1 Stuck Transactions:


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Most mining pools currently **do not mine** transactions with 0.1 sat/vB or similar ultra-low fee rates
    
*   Your transaction may remain **unconfirmed for days, weeks, or indefinitely**
    
*   **Funds become inaccessible** - you can't spend the same UTXOs until the transaction confirms
    
*   **P**articularly problematic for time-sensitive operations such as mint or trade
    

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-2-dust-utxo-attacks)

#2 Dust UTXO Attacks


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**How the Attack Works:**

*   **Malicious actors** send low-fee-rate UTXOs to your address
    
*   Later, your wallet automatically includes this UTXO when constructing a new transaction
    
*   The **entire transaction inherits the low fee rate**, making it unconfirmable
    
*   You must pay expensive RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration costs to fix the issue
    
*   Why it’s sneaky:
    
    *   Our wallet blocks UTXOs <600 sats, but attacks over 600 sats bypass this.
        
    *   Merging these UTXOs (via wallet tools) spreads the poison to new transactions.
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-3-transaction-chain-limitations)

#3: Transaction Chain Limitations

**The Technical Problem:**

*   Bitcoin's mempool has a **25-transaction ancestor limit**
    
*   Repeatedly spending 0.1 sat/vB transactions quickly approaches this limit
    
*   Once reached, **new transactions cannot be broadcast**
    
*   Regular users have **no way to resolve this** without technical tools
    

**Resolution Challenges:**

*   **Only solution** is using RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration tools to replace earlier transactions
    
*   **Current tool limitations** - many RBF implementations have bugs and don't handle data cleanup properly
    

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#recommendations-for-users)

🎯 Recommendations for Users

*   **Avoid sub-1 sat/vB transactions** unless you fully understand the risks
    
*   **Be Aware of the limited ecosystem support** for handling sub-1 sat/vB transactions properly and potential i**nconsistent behavior** across different wallet implementations
    
*   **Keep RBF tools available for emergency acceleration**
    

**How UniSat may support sub-1 sat/vB transactions**

*   We will do more research and aim to first implement in our explorer UniScan
    
*   More experimental tools may be possible in the future
    

More on how Sub-1 sat/vB transactions work: [https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions)

[PreviousWhat Happens When Bitcoin Fee Rates Drop Below 1 sat/vB?](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-when-bitcoin-fee-rates-drop-below-1-sat-vb)
[Nextbrc20-swap Introduction](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction)

# brc20-swap Introduction | UniSat

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction#the-brc20-swap-interface)

The brc20-swap interface


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can connect their brc-20 supported wallets to swap and provide liquidity on brc20-swap. These docs explain all the features of the app, and provide straightforward walkthroughs on how to use it.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FbHU5YXqZG6TslJhK89UA%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd63f7da5-c780-4e3f-8587-b996685ba0cc&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5ad0098d&sv=2)

The app consists of three pages:

**Swap** - the trading interface for executing swaps on brc20-swap and depositing more assets into the module.

**Pools** - the liquidity provider interface, where LPs can add liquidity to brc20-swap pools

**Transactions** \- interface for users to view the past brc20-swap interactions

brc20-swap operates like most decentralised exchanges: Users deposit assets into liquidity pools, where traders can exchange assets again at prices set by the AMM's math formula.

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction#connecting-your-wallet)

Connecting your wallet


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In order to swap or add liquidity on brc20-swap, you will first need a wallet with brc-20 support. These are available as an extension for popular browsers or as apps for your smartphone.

brc20-swap supports the following wallets:

*   [UniSat Wallet](https://unisat.io/download)
    

Click on any of the above links to find more information about each wallet, and instructions on how to install them on your browser or device.

Once you have installed a wallet, it’s time to connect it to brc20-swap.

When you first navigate to brc20-swap, you will see a button in the top right of your browser window that says **Connect**.

Click on this button and a modal will appear asking you to select a wallet. Choose the wallet you installed in the previous step.

At this point, the wallet app will take over and ask you to confirm the connection to brc20-swap. Your wallet is now connected to brc20-swap.

Read the testnet guide to learn how to prepare your wallet on testnet for testing brc20-swap

[Testnet guide](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/testnet-guide)

[](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction#depositing-assets-into-brc20-swap-module)

Depositing assets into brc20-swap module


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In order to swap or add liquidity on brc20-swap you must first deposit assets into the brc20-swap module balance.

Once you have connected to brc20-swap**,** switch to the Deposit tab in the swap page. Select the ticker for the assets you want to deposit into brc20-swap.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FH3KNXDJm2Pzrm5HaLHWN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1fcb65f0-50b8-4cd2-9214-5693cf87d1e1&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=38571537&sv=2)

Click on “inscribe TRANSFER”, UniSat Wallet will prompt you to sign an inscribe event.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FAnGvEyDvfXa3doXYSFDO%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfe78f2d9-2bbf-42b5-86d9-200772aa8365&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=26496d36&sv=2)

Your wallet will prompt you to enter an amount, enter the amount you wish to inscribe.

Sign the transaction, the transaction is broadcast to the network.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FNntjSQeN6eCyxOzAvrTV%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D206804b1-38d1-4b95-9a56-af7c8a3fcc56&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1acb055f&sv=2)

Click "Deposit" and sign the transfer inscription to brc20-swap. Once you must wait for 3 confirmation (which could take an hour) before the funds become available for brc20-swap.

[PreviousThe Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions)
[NextWhat Is an Automated Market Maker?](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/brc20-swap-introduction/what-is-an-automated-market-maker)

# Getting Started with FairPool | UniSat

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/fairpool/getting-started-with-fairpool#step-by-step-tutorial)

**Step-by-Step Tutorial**

**Step 1: Register an Account**

*   Visit [https://www.fairpool.network](https://www.fairpool.network/)
     and click on the "Register" button.
    
*   Fill in your username (Lowercase only) and password. It's recommended that you save this information for future reference.
    
*   You’ll also need to provide a Bitcoin address during registration. This is where your mining earnings will be sent, but don’t worry—you can update this address later if needed.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F6OHwxmTInGWmFn33A6gr%252F2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2c26af4e-cbb6-4806-a9fa-1ebc94a17442&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9afad25f&sv=2)

**Step 2: Configure your mining equipment settings**

Now that your account is set up, it’s time to configure your miners to connect to FairPool:

*   Go to the homepage of FairPool and find the "Mining Address" section.
    
    *   For Fractal Mainnet - Copy the mining pool address: `stratum+tcp://pool-solo.fairpool.network:3333`
        
    *   For Fractal Testnet - Copy the mining pool address: `stratum+tcp://pool-solo-t1.fairpool.network:3333`
        
    

In your mining equipment’s settings, input the following details:

*   **Pool Address for Mainnet**: `pool-solo.fairpool.network:3333`
    
*   **Pool Address for Testnet:** `pool-solo-t1.fairpool.network:3333`
    
*   **Username:** Name your miner in the format `user_name.worker_name`, where `user_name` is the username you registered with in the first step, for example: `alice.x01`(Lowercase only) . The `worker_name` is the name of your mining machine, but this is not mandatory.
    
*   **Password:** Leave this field empty; it’s not required.
    

After connecting, you should see your miners’ real-time hashrate displayed on FairPool’s homepage, confirming that you’re successfully mining.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F40UpSn29UnjNwGtgNVRa%252F7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbcfb2abc-f033-4600-acb2-bee2d8ab2048&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=12d38601&sv=2)

**Step 3: Monitor and Receive Your Earnings**

Once your miners are up and running, here’s how you’ll receive your earnings:

*   **Daily Settlement:** Your earnings are calculated and finalized daily at 00:00 (UTC).
    
*   **Automatic Payouts:** At 06:00 (UTC) per day, your earnings will be automatically sent to the Bitcoin address you registered with.
    
*   **Check Your Balance:** You can log in to your FairPool account anytime to check your current balance and review your earnings history.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FyxqbGBMANeun766Vxdn0%252F8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D63849e91-4298-4401-bfe3-cf9d47a49c8a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8fcc60e8&sv=2)

[PreviousFairPool](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/fairpool)

Last updated 9 months ago

# How to Submit Collection in GitHub? | UniSat

This document provides a detailed guide for project teams on how to submit an application to **list new collections** on the UniSat Marketplace on Fractal.

1.  Prepare the contents of the two files, `meta.json` and `inscriptions.json`, for the collection.
    
2.  Sign in to GitHub and open [https://github.com/unisat-wallet/fractal-ordinals-collections](https://github.com/unisat-wallet/fractal-ordinals-collections)
     (templates for `meta.json` and `inscriptions.json` are available on this page).
    
3.  Click "Fork" on the page.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fnkxgj3Nq0uSRIxWXse85%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7c6e4c95-3ea9-4752-a7fa-51e00f381229&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=84dd1e41&sv=2)

1.  It will automatically load the info for "Owner" and "Repository name" on the next page. Then click "Create fork".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F3ZfhKrbYhhju1UEZmpPL%252F2.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0df01dad-0e5d-4a75-9eaf-a8f1906d44d8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=16e68dd1&sv=2)

1.  Wait a few seconds for the fork to be created. Once done, click "collections".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FqSlaxec25QA6miHGWuBw%252F3.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D796d55a1-ed86-4d1c-8e35-29f406b1279b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=61aec76b&sv=2)

1.  Click "Add file" -> "Create new file".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FpgnC5ytxSCTo4BOnOmQq%252F4.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd287e354-2b81-4fea-b610-693f6f187b5f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f1e285df&sv=2)

1.  In the textbox below, create your collection folder. **NOTE:** The folder name must end with a `/`, for example, `test1/`. The folder name is the slug in the conllections meta.json.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FVgAeBreWfwiJbL11x8pQ%252F5.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddec8e7de-1415-4a6f-987d-79256859e414&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=397b3593&sv=2)

1.  Create the file under the collection folder, enter `meta.json` in the textbox after the folder name as shown below, then copy/paste the related content of `meta.json` into the edit box. Finally, click "Commit changes...".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FNsN4n1DyOaP79mlWFJfw%252F6.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7d2e7bed-3e51-4305-bd06-4bf0e862760e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7a3df6e3&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FXQb0187hazIUKT1Yl7zN%252F7.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De72d2146-f98b-4d6f-9a4e-ef9f7809bb48&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fff42dc8&sv=2)

1.  You can check the left column to confirm that the `meta.json` file was created successfully.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FrR3IgUV89gI9V4UF5M51%252F8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D28c7f6cd-ac0f-473c-80d0-79107fb37b61&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c2d16078&sv=2)

1.  Use the same method to create the second file, `inscriptions.json`.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fvm73ZcSvenuv1BEuQWnW%252F9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6f6d7945-fb0c-4c44-a579-716778e5d060&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c9cbbb4f&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fk254VwxiurjvFq9fg78x%252F10.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dce933454-9942-4f09-9c4e-c05473d4df9b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6c5f9dcf&sv=2)

1.  Once both files are added, click the "Pull requests" tab -> "New pull request".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FUKwNWXUw1X26KuUNYIdM%252F11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc2e392d4-b8dd-4ee1-b8b8-9cbb62916f3e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=15cc7734&sv=2)

1.  If the page shows a green "Able to merge" message, click "Create pull request".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fj124tsCx4Jdg5DVbzfbw%252F12.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D24a6d616-205c-4312-9b1c-bc99f714a526&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9a9b373d&sv=2)

1.  Add a title and description (optional), then click "Create pull request".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F6vNhSDHpbGTUZ5HbEh8y%252F13.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbc3c64cd-4878-4953-9405-36a7fb8536aa&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5b27a701&sv=2)

1.  All done! You can find your request listed under "Pull requests".
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F3aXzULVdLPMttVAMXRo9%252F14.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0a360ee0-0345-4e4d-9c23-41927aefaaa3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d805dfb8&sv=2)

**Please keep the following in mind when submitting your request**:

*   Be patient while we process your request.
    
*   Pay attention to the comments in your request. If your submission doesn't meet the requirements, we will specify the reason, and requests with invalid JSON files will be closed.
    
*   Do not repeatedly submit requests.
    
*   Submit a complete collection in one request. Do not spread files across multiple requests.
    
*   Do not submit multiple collections in one request. If one collection doesn't meet the criteria, it could affect the approval of others in the same request.

# Open API Documentation | UniSat

Please read [Developer Service Legal Disclaimer](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/developer-center/developer-service-legal-disclaimer)
 before using the OpenAPI below.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FrItWXkDwExIiAXvWKX8M%252F20240516-175257.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De1bf87fe-af60-47e9-a6d0-6342967180b0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=71396bf6&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/open-api-documentation#overview)

Overview

UniSat Developer Service is open to community developers, allowing you to explore the world of Bitcoin and ordinals. You can deploy your own inscribing services, build wallet applications, develop browsers, and much more using the API.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/open-api-documentation#getting-an-api-key)

Getting an API Key

To use the OpenAPI, please register and log in at the [UniSat Developer Center](https://developer.unisat.io/)
. Once registered, you can directly obtain a free-plan API key through the developer center.

When you obtain the API key, please add it to the request header with the `Authorization` format as follows:

Copy

    curl -X 'GET' \
      'https://open-api.unisat.io/v1/indexer/blockchain/info' \
      -H 'accept: application/json' \
      -H 'Authorization: Bearer YOUR_API_KEY'

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/open-api-documentation#endpoint-urls)

Endpoint URLs

Network

URL

Swagger

Mainnet

https://open-api.unisat.io https://open-api-s1.unisat.io (Only WhiteList)

[https://open-api.unisat.io/swagger.html](https://open-api.unisat.io/swagger.html)

Testnet

https://open-api-testnet.unisat.io

[https://open-api-testnet.unisat.io/swagger.html](https://open-api-testnet.unisat.io/swagger.html)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/open-api-documentation#rate-limits)

Rate Limits

API Tier

Rate Limit

Free

5 calls/second , up to 2,000 calls/day

If you require higher limits than those provided by our free plan, you can directly purchase a higher-tier plan through the [UniSat Developer Center](https://developer.unisat.io/plan)
.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/dev/open-api-documentation#issues-and-feature-requests)

Issues & Feature Requests

For issue reports and feature requests, please visit the repository below:

*   [https://github.com/unisat-wallet/unisat-dev-support/issues](https://github.com/unisat-wallet/unisat-dev-support/issues)

# How to send / receive CAT20? | UniSat

**Step 1: Download the Chrome Extension**

• **Download UniSat Wallet**: Visit the official Chrome Web Store link for **UniSat Wallet** and verify that it has a large number of reviews and a verified checkmark to ensure it’s not a phishing site. Download link: [Here](https://unisat.io/download)

_Make sure you are using the latest version of the extension, which must be at least v1.5.0 or higher._

**Step 2: Set Up Your Wallet**

• Install the extension and **set up your wallet**. During the setup process, **securely back up your seed phrase** and make sure **not to share** it or store it online.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FOjji4BdA1cxAcXAAOuR7%252F11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D45257141-c48f-41fa-8f97-6551d7d0052e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=41f196e0&sv=2)

**Step 3: Select a Taproot Address**

• Ensure that you select a **Taproot address** to be compatible with Fractal Bitcoin.

Only **Taproot and Native Segwit** wallet addresses are supported to transfer CAT20 tickers.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fwwu1BTOXQutpvQa3NLQh%252F22.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da6889e65-29fc-4c83-b7a6-b2935d3d7a9a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=98e5ad97&sv=2)

**Step 4: Toggle to Fractal Bitcoin**• In the wallet interface, navigate to the **top-right corner** and switch from **BTC Mainnet** to **Fractal Bitcoin Mainnet**.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FAvfXDT8e9m1iwK9xQiYW%252F33.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1f35910b-2c5b-41d5-9cc0-c237501f87b1&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d3fb69b6&sv=2)

**Step 5: Check Your CAT20 Balance**

• Once you’ve toggled to **Fractal Bitcoin**, your balance will be displayed.

• To **receive CAT20**, click **Receive** and copy your Fractal Bitcoin receiving address to share with others.(Taproot and Native Segwit wallet addresses only)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FdRsf0566zCKuSxqz96hn%252F44.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De14b1d70-a18a-4835-95d9-89db3ec40706&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2a6541d5&sv=2)

**Step 6: Send CAT20**

*   To **send CAT20**, please click on the specific **CAT20 ticker** you want to send and then click on Send.
    
*   Carefully review the transaction details, including **inputs** and **outputs**, before confirming. Once verified, click **Next** and sign the transaction.
    

> **Note**: You can send up to **4 UTXOs** in one transaction. After sending, the UTXOs will automatically merge into one.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FJT1xrOTZt0H0CKs9gu0p%252F2-3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D786e1269-95ce-4e5b-9b88-c217f9fb6d68&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=428fe23f&sv=2)

* * *

**How to Merge CAT20 UTXOs**

Merging multiple CAT20 UTXOs into a single UTXO can only be done if they share the same genesis transaction. Follow these steps to merge your UTXOs:

**Step 1: Select the CAT20 Ticker**

Select the CAT20 TickerClick on the specific **CAT20 ticker** you want to merge. In the pop-up menu, select **Merge UTXOs**.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fm1M3WbNggRKatevTQ44s%252F4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Daa98cbe4-7e43-4b98-a461-1e51cdbe82a8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fdab62ec&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-send-receive-cat20#step-2-choose-utxos-to-merge)

**Step 2: Choose UTXOs to Merge**

*   In the **Merge** window, select the number of UTXOs you wish to merge and set your fee rate.
    
*   Review the transaction details to ensure accuracy, then click **Start Merging** to initiate the merging process.
    

> **Note**: You can merge up to **100 UTXOs** in one go.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FZEwXLujssJYFmBozGJsl%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbffeb6b3-a241-4643-bb73-370142ce4210&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=daa7ee88&sv=2)

**Step 3: Confirm and Start the Merge**

*   Once you’ve reviewed all the details, click **Start** to begin the UTXO merge. After the transaction is confirmed, you’ll see the progress in the wallet interface.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F5u6RZuigCuGRICj6P1s9%252F5-6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb0e654f-eb51-4a68-afc4-830d4928ae9e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e2433c7c&sv=2)

[PreviousCAT on Fractal](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal)
[NextHow to Buy and Sell CAT on UniSat CAT Market？](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market)

# Transfer brc-20 in UniSat Wallet (2023) | UniSat

UniSat Wallet now supports TRANSFER of brc-20 since 1.1.15. (available here: [Google Chrome Store](https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/ppbibelpcjmhbdihakflkdcoccbgbkpo)
)

Please follow the step-by-step guide below to learn how to transfer your brc-20 to others.

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-3af9)

1\. Make sure the version of Unisat is the latest.

*   Switch to the 'Settings' tab and scroll to the bottom.
    
*   Verify the version number to make sure it’s the latest, current is **1.4.5 .**
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FcuPiVtMDN31DytmNmW49%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbde17c96-9d6e-4a9b-9703-05013252b54e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=82953930&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-6bcf)

2\. Switch to the ‘Home’ tab and click the ‘brc-20’ tag

Each volumn here represents a specific brc-20 tick (like ‘sats’), containing multiple associated inscriptions.Please note that the balance contains two parts:

*   **Transferable**: The amount here has been inscribed into one or more TRANSFER inscriptions (can be transferred immediately).
    
*   **Available**: The amount here is available as a part of your balance (including both minted and received) **but not transferable yet**. To spend it, you must first inscribe a certain amount into a TRANSFER inscription.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FOJRNNpJgCGwt06cLYW2C%252F2.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0deccf4e-0183-4c3d-9149-50265e49ad18&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e53599fc&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#e624)

3\. Click one of your brc-20s to check out the details.

*   All your associated inscriptions are listed here.
    
*   The green ones are transferable (please note we have no transferable inscription yet on the screenshot below).
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F7CPypJ1ssguvIbGMHW5c%252F3.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb37627e-2234-4998-b57a-0a52237e22e3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b27a42a3&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-33b2)

4\. Click ‘TRANSFER’ to enter the transfer process.

*   All transferable inscriptions are listed here for you to choose from.
    
*   The transfer Amount is not an editable field. It can only be calculated by the sum of the chosen amounts of TRANSFER inscriptions.
    
*   If you don’t have enough transferable inscriptions yet, you are going to inscribe them first.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FKBjawFIcRl3jn9ic2tsQ%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb9dc8e6-3299-42ca-beac-2303a138833b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8a548979&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-85eb)

5\. Click the ‘Inscribe TRANSFER’ button.

*   Input the amount that you want to inscribe into a TRANSFER inscription.
    
*   Choose an appropriate fee rate.
    
*   And click the ‘Inscribe TRANSFER’ button on the bottom.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FvmTTTK9K0rNLmwfHNCfn%252F6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8157dae1-6446-4ac8-bc73-0ec89e9e7f48&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=acc9baf3&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#e3b8)

6\. Preview the details of the TRANSFER inscription and click ‘Pay & Inscribe’ to execute

*   You may return to the earlier steps by clicking the back button and changing values and settings before submitting.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FHdnT6vYYn3AOF6Tk9Fif%252F7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd114b993-d461-40e6-90f0-52704a826d7d&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4a0dffb9&sv=2)

Preview TRANSFER

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FZTZlJCXy7PyxltvRI3iX%252F8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3c9ca91c-24aa-4df9-8364-a641452bb39b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7a099d78&sv=2)

Sign & Pay for transfer

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#a257)

7\. Choose a TRANSFER inscription and proceed to step 2

*   Once a number of TRANSFER inscriptions are chosen, we can proceed to send them to the receiver by typing its address (or .sats name)
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F3Beh3SQQipQEuJT39IYw%252F9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc37edd8e-65d2-46b8-b0f4-809d5f62f382&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7dc6b66d&sv=2)

Choose TRANSFER and click ‘Next’

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FLkY4K9e7mNRpJGvyzSM9%252F10.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3993f5b0-0633-4b2f-9b26-49cb6656743a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=738a27d7&sv=2)

Input the address or .unisat name of the receiver

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-0c70)

8\. Preview the transaction before sending.

*   Click ‘Sign & Send’ to perform the transfer operation eventually.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F5ewMLf4n28ByeTlavhjq%252F11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dde494cd8-210b-4da0-a86c-4ad297539523&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d9268c65&sv=2)

Preview the transaction before sending

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/deprecated/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-2164)

9\. Congratulations! The transfer is now completed!

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FwokyEoKz56iRREpVSJqs%252F12.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D208ea52b-d448-4807-ad53-57ec56ce1f07&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=947811c4&sv=2)

*   UniSat Wallet: [https://unisat.io/](https://unisat.io/)
    
*   brc20 spec: [https://domo-2.gitbook.io/brc-20-experiment/](https://domo-2.gitbook.io/brc-20-experiment/)
    

If you have questions, just ask on our Discord server: [https://discord.gg/EMskB2sMz8](https://discord.gg/EMskB2sMz8)

Happy inscribing and transferring!

UniSat Team (2024–09–02)

# How to Buy and Sell CAT on UniSat CAT Market？ | UniSat

In this guide, we'll walk you through the process of buying and selling CAT on the UniSat CAT Market. Please note, this guide is for reference purposes only, and we encourage you to do your own research before trading.

* * *

CAT Market is compatible with **Native Segwit (P2WPKH)** and **Taproot (P2TR)** addresses on UniSat. Make sure your wallet is configured to use one of these address formats.

Transaction fees are paid in FB

Service fee: 0.3%

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#id-1.-accessing-unisat-cat-market)

**1\. Accessing UniSat CAT Market**

*   Go to the UniSat Marketplace on Fractal: [https://fractal.unisat.io/dex/cat20](https://fractal.unisat.io/dex/cat20)
    
*   Click the **Connect** button to link your wallet to the marketplace.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FIrCbgGEatKeYQLyIK9VV%252F11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc7bfe032-ffc4-4269-85f4-247d92d9aac0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5943c6e3&sv=2)

The CAT Market interface is designed with a DEX-style layout to suit the trading preferences of most users. Click on the specific ticker you want to trade, and you’ll be able to see its **price**, **price chart**, **volume**, and **market cap** for better insights into your asset.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FgEJiPGepzAqy2orpzxMk%252F444.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3f409ca0-f12c-4039-8a01-88c8b835c7ba&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b803462d&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#id-2.-how-to-buy-cat)

2\. How to Buy CAT

Use the search bar on the right side of the market interface to find the ticker you wish to trade with, or scroll to find it directly.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FNOlBto5YYSwaumLT7Wvz%252F22.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2e6b8df9-ef24-4bd7-8688-8dafdb9ec5ee&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5e4ac1a9&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#buying-method-1-take-order)

**Buying Method 1: Take Order**

This is a fast way to buy from the existing order book.

a) Click on the desired buy order from the order book (buy side) that matches your preferred price and amount, confirm the details (price and amount), and click the **Buy** button at the bottom of the page.

b) Review the **inputs** and **outputs** information, and if everything looks correct, sign the transaction.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FeFQelk17Q8EFxz2rTeF5%252F33.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D01345e78-1fbe-4105-8948-c8d5da9551ea&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8a60351f&sv=2)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FxTLzXs17OylP0v8XZtsI%252F44-55.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D116b6027-5316-4a7a-beee-0351276da7d4&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d475771e&sv=2)

Once the transaction is signed and confirmed, the purchase will be processed. You can view your purchase history under the **My Activities** section at the bottom of the page.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F2RoREFqpnNNN5rlWMLri%252F66.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5c58f2a9-d125-4a50-a3c7-b353674bfce2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7dc4861e&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#buying-method-2-make-order)

**Buying Method 2: Make Order**

If you prefer to place a custom order instead of buying from the existing order book, follow these steps:

a) Choose **Make Order**, then click **Buy**.

b) Enter your ideal buy price and quantity, and confirm the details before clicking **Make Order**.

_Note: the total value should be bigger than 0.1 FB._

c) As in the first method, review the transaction details (inputs, outputs), and sign it to confirm the order.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FXluiRV1JP9RTmzLhUyQO%252F77.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db6d3741b-3037-469c-bdb4-92f47fae2483&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=737f1076&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#bulk-buy)

**Bulk Buy**

You can select multiple orders for bulk purchasing:

*   Click **Take Order - Buy** on the marketplace, and choose multiple orders from the order book.
    
*   Once selected, click **Buy** and sign the transaction to complete the purchase.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FHnaHoIuI47onBikDb3nr%252F222.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D367699f5-6834-4b9b-ab1f-eb149ea27682&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a60f1bd9&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#id-3.-how-to-sell-cat)

3\. How to Sell CAT

Use the search bar or scroll through the marketplace to find the ticker you want to sell.

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#selling-method-1-take-order)

**Selling Method 1: Take Order**

This is a fast way to sell by accepting an existing buy order from the order book.

a) Click on the available sell order (sell side) in the order book that matches your desired price and quantity.

b) Confirm the price and quantity, and click **Sell** at the bottom of the page.

c) Review the inputs and outputs information, then sign the transaction.

**Note:** You can place up to 3 orders in bulk.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FqUPjIL7XfNMBrbYXz1Sv%252F99.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D02dcac4e-7c7e-4339-967b-23aef8424e78&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bcc6fae6&sv=2)

**Selling Method 2: Make Order**

If you prefer to place a sell order instead of taking one from the existing order book:

You can sell up to **3 UTXOs at once**. If you wish to sell more CAT20 in one go, you need to merge the UTXOs in your wallet.

For detailed steps on how to do this, please refer to this operation guide.

[![Logo](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Ficon%252FLCxttftJ8BHboA7PLsfL%252Ftwitter%2520PFP%2520800x800%2520px.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbcf931af-88e1-41ca-b576-3efc1b6ec166&width=20&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=baba8c6d&sv=2)How to send / receive CAT20? | UniSat](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-services/cat-support/how-to-send-receive-cat20)

a) Choose **Make Order**, then click **Sell**.

b) Enter the quantity and price you wish to sell for, and confirm the details before clicking **Make Sell**.

_Note: the total value should be bigger than 0.1 FB._

c) As in the previous steps, review the transaction information (inputs, outputs), and sign to confirm the order.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FA80yl4YU2IKiVawtzQNu%252F111.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd1dba5cc-946d-4320-bd2e-874edd554002&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e1578ba0&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#bulk-sell)

**Bulk Sell**

You can also sell multiple UTXOs in one go:

*   Click **Take Order - Sell**.
    
*   Select the orders you wish to fulfill, click **Sell**, and sign the transaction to complete it.
    
*   Note: You can sell up to 3 UTXOs at once.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252Fa64nfmcXVmK25BTvY67P%252F333.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbd94f77b-3b63-4bfb-8acd-1d92196ee1e6&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3851441c&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-buy-and-sell-cat-on-unisat-cat-market#id-4.-how-to-view-and-cancel-orders)

4\. How to View and Cancel Orders

After placing your orders, you can view your order history under **My Activities** on the main page.

To cancel an open order, click the **Cancel** button next to the order you wish to remove.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FnlkxWRG6rufabspQevS5%252F78.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6971f939-a9e4-47cb-a3f4-43ce1b93799e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=85ca6850&sv=2)

**Please note:**

CAT20 transactions require confirmed UTXOs. If there are multiple unconfirmed UTXOs in your orders, you will not be able to spend the same UTXO again. In such cases, the page will display the following prompt. Please click "Confirm" to proceed to the next step.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FcFeUncPHWtfQ6Ol7f91g%252F79.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D46790a55-f9ab-4056-bb78-2d6d23783640&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a7fe113&sv=2)

[PreviousHow to send / receive CAT20?](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/cat-on-fractal/how-to-send-receive-cat20)
[NextFractal Service Links](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/fractal-service-links)
